NEURICE  3 
1. Excellence
1.1 Objectives  
The main objective of the project is to d evelop strategies for rice productivity, stability and quality by developing New 
commercial EUropean RICE (Oryza sativa) harbouring salt tolerance alleles to protect the rice sector against climate change and 
apple snail (Pomacea insularum) invasion (NEURICE). 
European rice consumption was ca. 2.68 million tonnes of milled rice (Mt) in 2014, while the rice production in Europe (EU-28) 
for the same year was ca. 1.64 Mt [1], being mainly temperate japonica rice. The rice production from 2013 to 2014 decreased 
from 1.77 Mt to 1.64 Mt, consequently, the rice imports have increased from 0.9 Mt in 2013 to 1.1 Mt in 2014, being mainly long-
grain indica rice. The rice exports (mainly japonica rice) were maintained at 0.2 Mt [1]. Thus, only 61% of the rice consumed by 
European citizens in 2014 was produced in EU [1]. European rice productivity is affected by abiotic and biotic stresses and by 
the local farming practices.  
Current European rice Genotypes are not able to withstand salinity increases  that the Environment is posing on the rice 
producing regions due to climate change , moreover poor Management has been employed to afford this in a proper way. Of 
particular concern, global temperature has increased over the last century, especially during the last 50 years (0.13° C / decade). 
This warming has been more intense in the Mediterranean region [2], and has been specially evident in spring and summer. 
Temperature increases around the Mediterranean coasts are greater than that observed in other regions of the same latitude. In 
addition, due to scarcer water availability and the rise in sea levels, there is a clear tendency toward salinization in the river 
deltas where rice is grown in Europe, notably in the plots close to the sea level [2]. Salinization certainly affects rice as it is the 
most salt sensitive crop among cereals [3, 4].  
Associated with changes in temperature, the biotic stress of the Apple snail species from genus Pomacea now threatens to 
destroy Europe’s rice paddy fields eating the sown seed and the rice plantlets, representing one of the worst introduced gastropod 
crop pest of the recent time [5-10]. It is calculated that nowadays this pest causes damages in rice fields worldwide that result 
into losses of tens of billions of Euros a year [11]. Recently, apple snails have been detected in the Ebro river delta, and now 
it represents an important thread to Europe’s wetlands biodiversity and rice production. To date the measures adopted to 
combat apple snail have failed, but in the autumn of 2013 a new strategy with permission of the EU was explored, which consisted 
in flooding 2500 ha of infested fields with seawater  to eradicate the  apple snails . This treatment proved 100% effective in 
destroying apple snail infestations [12], nevertheless residual salt concentrations affected negatively rice productivity. There is a 
way to bypass this problem, which is to introgress salt tolerance into elite European varieties using the most salt resistance alleles 
from tolerant rice lines such as Pokkali, FL478 and IR64-Saltol. It has been reported that Pokkali and FL478 can grow at 150 mM 
NaCl concentrations [13], while the most salt tolerant European cultivars just can tolerate  salinity ranges between 30 and 60 mM. 
The European deltaic areas have been historically and naturally salinized before rice cultivation, when artificial inundation during 
the dry season (summer) reduced salinity levels to per mit rice cultivation, thus the natural flora and fauna are not negatively 
affected by the seawater treatment.  
The NEURICE project proposes a coordinated multi-actor approach  that includes public research and technological 
development universities and the active participation of end-users such as technological companies, a specialized technological 
centre for breeding and innovation support and farmers cooperatives . The NEURICE project aims t o address rice abiotic (i.e. 
salinity in fields caused by rise in seawater level and scarce of water availability due to climatic change effects) and biotic (i.e. 
apple snail pest) stresses. T he project ensures the generation and growth of ideas between all the partners to develop the co -
creation and the co-ownership of new knowledge, technologies and techniques that will facilitate their adoption for the benefit of 
the rice production sector as well as the generation of more jobs in Europe.  
  
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  4 
Thus, the general objective of the NEURICE project is to identify and introduc e genetic variation in European rice 
varieties for obtaining commercial varieties tolerant to salinity in order to:  
(i) mitigate the imminent effects of salinization and deterioration of water quality in the Mediterranean basins due to 
climate change; and  
(ii) avoid the decline in production observed after seawater treatments performed in rice paddies that successfully 
controlled the apple snail pest (which has recently appeared in a major producing region of Europe, the Ebro delta) 
but it is likely to spread to other rice growing areas in Europe producing great loses [14].  
For the seed industry partners from participated countries, the final objective of the NEURICE project  is to register and 
commercialize new s alt tolerant elite European lines . These new salt tolerant European commercial l ines will become 
available all over Europe to use them as prevention to abiotic stress derived from climate change as well as for avoiding 
the dispersion of this devastating pest ( biotic stress ) apple snail  all over Europe  while maintaining or increasing rice 
production. These new rice lines will allow rice cultivation in abandoned salinized paddies, while low productive salinized 
fields will obtain higher yields resulting in creation of new jobs and a reduction of the rice import in Europe 
The specific objectives of the NEURICE project are:  
1. To identify new salt tolerant varieties and new salt tolerance alleles  using phenotypical, physiological and genetic 
screening of germplasm collection and complementary approaches of Genome Wide Association Study (GWAS) in a panel 
of japonica accessions and linkage mapping in a population of  biparental Recombinant Inbred Lines (RILs) (UMIL, CRA, 
UGLA, INDEAR and CAAS). The partners selected for this proposal include European teams with outstanding expertise in 
rice geno typing/phenotyping and top worldwide teams in biotechnology from third -country partners (i.e. Argentina and 
People’s Republic of China).  By the 24th month of the NEURICE project , salt tolerant japonica accessions and biparental 
RILs will be identified, moreover at the month 48 the genomic studies will be complete. 
2. To obtain advanced lines with improved salt tolerance  by introgressing Saltol, a chromosome segment carrying a salt 
tolerance gene from the highly salt tolerant Asian variety FL478 into European elite varieties from Spain, Italy and France 
using marker assisted backcross (MABC) selection (UB, UMIL, CRAG, CIRAD, CRA, UGLA and CFR). This objective also 
includes an embryo rescue adaptation to fasten the (MABC) process. The best rice centres from the m ain rice production 
areas have been carefully selected as partners. At the 22th month of the project, BC3F3 seeds (the 3rd generation of the 3rd 
backcross) will be ready to be assayed in controlled conditions using hydroponic systems to validate their salinity tolerance. 
3. To evaluate salinity tolerance in controlled conditions using hydroponic systems  to validate salt tolerant lines 
produced within this project after introgressing salt tolerance genes from FL478 into the European elite varieties (UB, CRAG, 
CIRAD, UMIL and UGLA),  including the most salt tolerant japonica accessions and RILs . This evaluation will be 
complemented with the  quantification of  salinity-related transport and accumulation traits (UGLA)  and oxidative stress 
markers (UB). The seeds from the validated lines will be obtained in the month 27 to be used in the field trials under non-
salinized and salinized conditions. 
4. To perform field trials to evaluate in salinized and non-salinized conditions the traditional European rice lines 
harbouring the Saltol salt tolerance chromosomal region introgressed from salt tolerant FL478, as well as the most salt 
tolerant japonica accessions and RILs, in order to select those  salt tolerant lines with commercial potential. Each country 
will assess their lines in their low salinity environmental conditions to ensure quality, productivity and commerciality of lines 
(CAMARA in Spain, CRA in Italy and CFR in France). In parallel, the same lines will be assessed in high salinity conditions 
field trials (IRTA in Spain, SIS in Italy and CFR in France). Samples from lines assessed in both salinity levels will be studied 
in order to select those salt tolerant lines with best commercial potentiality with the objective of registering  the best for 
commercialization. Selection will take into account productivity and quality for both industrial (head rice recovery, grain length 
and width, amylose content, etc.) and nutritional  traits such as storage of microelements essential for human diet such as 
Fe and Zn, exclusion of toxic heavy metal such as Cd and As (UB, IRTA, CAMARA, IRIS and UMIL). The competent partners 
from each country will commercialize these lines. Thus,  the NEURICE consortium will ensure that the obtained lines 
maintain, or even increase, the actual productivity of parental lines. 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  5 
5. To implement a s alinity motorization system in rice plots treated with seawater  using a novel autonomous salinity 
wireless sensor network based on low cost sensors developed by IRIS, which is a company specialised in monitoring 
technologies with several years of experience in the agricultural sector. Sensors will be placed in all plots dedicated to low 
and high salinity field trials in order to monitor continuously their salinity levels. This remote data transmission system will 
have a software package including a data-mining layer in which all the data collected in the fields will be used for improving 
the management of irrigation through a decision support system. This information will serve to evaluate in real time the 
impact of the proposed adaptability interventions in response salinity levels while ensuring the productivity and stability of 
the agricultural sector. 
6. To transfer the knowledge of the new elite European salt tolerant varieties and the salinity monitorization system to the 
end users through extensive open field days as well as seminars and other instances intended to disseminate and 
communicate the results and goods obtained in the NEURICE project . Knowledge transfer will allow the end-users of the 
rice sector, which are primarily rice farmers, rice farmers associations, rice farmer’s cooperatives and the rice seed industry, 
to properly implement the new salt tolerant varieties as well as the salinity monitorization system.
1.2 Relation to the work programme  
The NEURICE project, presented within the call Sustainable Food Security and the sub-call of: H2020-SFS-2014-2015 
and Topic: Strategies for crop productivity, stability and quality SFS-05-2015, explicitly considers improving identification, 
prediction and introduction of useful genetic variation in crops while seeking for novel breeding targets to improve yield, yield stability, 
quality, biotic/abiotic stress resistance/tolerance and environmental benefits. 
The proposal falls into the concept of multi-actor approach that includes rice farmer’s cooperatives, rice institutions and SMEs 
(CAMARA, CFR, SIS ), RTD public organizations (U B, CRAG, CIRAD, CRA, UMIL, UGLA, IRTA  and CAAS), an SME of the 
agrobiotechnology sector (INDEAR). They all have the equipment and human capital to approach crop improvement with advanced 
molecular breeding procedures to face climate change and apple snail problems. In addition, a private company (IRIS) specialized 
in developing low cost and high effective remote detection devices will develop a remote wireless sensor network to monitor salinity. 
Moreover, the NEURICE proposal is based on an international cooperation in research and innovation that includes countries 
like Argentina and People’s Republic of China  of which cent res involved in the NEURICE project are experts in the fields of 
genomics and bioinformatics, respectively. Furthermore, these two countries are great rice producers so they will be of uttermost 
importance to the project to disseminate the new salinity elite European tolerant lines produced in this project and to commercialize 
them outside of the Europe region. 
The project proposes smart approaches and tools to improve identification, prediction and introduction of salt tolerance variation 
into European rice cultivars, while monitoring salt concentrations. The salt tolerance improvement of rice varieties is tackled in a 
holistic manner, seeking for new salt tolerance alleles, and developing new material introgressed with the most salt tolerant gene 
alleles that have been recently identified in rice [15]. The novel breeding targets, other than yield stability, include the 
maintenance/improvement under mild salt stress tolerance of nutritional and industrial rice grain qualitative traits. 
The NEURICE project is a trans-disciplinary approach that integrate:  
1. Non-academic knowledge from f armer and Rice breeding knowledge  through SME farmer’s cooperative 
(CAMARA), SME rice institution (CFR), SME rice private company (SIS) and RTD public organizations (CIRAD, CRA, 
IRTA) that work with direct contact with farmer’s reality. This farmers-institutions close interaction will contribute to solve 
complex problems while fostering multi-actor engagement in the research and innovation process 
2. Plant physiology expertise from Universities with expertise in salt stress at physiological and subcellular level (U B, 
UMIL, UGLA). 
3. Plant biotechnology knowledge and expertise from RTD public organizations (CIRAD, CRA) and SMEs (CFR, SIS , 
INDEAR). 
4. Expertise in genomic, transcriptomic and data analysis from RTD public organizations (CRAG, CRA, CAAS), SME 
of agrobiotechnology sector (INDEAR). 
5. Knowledge in sensor reading, process logic and control, modelling from the SME private company (IRIS). 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  6 
6. Market knowledge and positioning to protect IP and successfully commercialize the derived products from the project 
(CRA, CAMARA, IRIS, CFR, SIS). 
Our project has been developed based in the farmer needs through addressing breeding programmes and farm management to 
help minimizing yield losses due to salinity through introducing salt tolerance to the European rice varieties. Abiotic stresses 
such as salinity are highly damaging to rice due to its salt sensitivity. In this context, climate change is expected to salinize fields 
due to the temperature  increase, sea levels rise, and reduced precipitation [2]. Hence, it is crucial to introduce salt tolerance 
alleles to European rice varieties to be prepared for this forthcoming scenario. In addition, global warming clearly set to enhance 
invasions by tropical species (biotic stresses), such as the apple snail ( Pomacea insularum) as they expand into new habitats 
[16]. Accidentally, the apple snail was recently been introduced in Europe (as in other Asian countries) , producing severe 
rice yield losses  [9-11, 17-19], This species is considered one of the worse introduced gastropod crop pest of the recent time 
and has been identified as a new pest by the European Food Safety Authority [14]. Seawater flooding has proved an efficient 
means to eradicate apple snails from infested fields. However, European rice genotypes are highly salt sensitive and application 
of such eradicating procedure in fields have led to a 30% loss of productivity [20]. Fighting the apple snail in rice fields with 
seawater has proved to be more effective than any other treatments (i.e. chemical), while preserving environment and biodiversity 
in wetlands (bird species, invertebrates, fisheries and aquiculture industry).
1.3 Concept and approach 
 1.3.1 Main ideas of the project (state-of-art) 
European rice cultivation importance. Rice (Oryza sativa) is one of the most important cereal crops in the world, and makes up 
an important calorie proportion of the human diet. Europe produces  1.64 Mt of rice which represents a 61% of the 2.68 Mt of 
milled rice consumed in Europe [1]. Rice production thus has major socio -cultural, economic and ecological impacts in several 
European Mediterranean countries. These countries have adapted their gastronomy to locally produced varieties, in general of 
short and pearl -shaped grain, which are the best suited for paella or risotto recipes. In Europe, Spain a nd Italy are by far the 
biggest European producers (80% production). However, several other countries are also rice producers, including France among 
others, which along with Spain and Italy have several Research Centres, Universities, rice farmer associations and cooperatives 
and rice seed industries working on increasing quality and productivity among their elite cultivated lines 
(http://ec.europa.eu/agriculture/markets/rice/index_en.htm). Increasing and promoting rice cul tivation in Europe is of the ut most 
importance to increase production and thereby decrease imports as well as for maintaining the derived commerce from the rice 
sector such as tourism and gastronomy. 
Rice salt sensitiveness. Rice is one of the most salt sensitive crops [4, 21]. Salinity affects both its early growth and reproductive 
stages, delaying the blooming time and reducing the pollen viability which negatively affects the productivity. Yield is affe cted 
even under mild salinity : an electroconductivity of about 2.6 dS/m reduced the yield to 90 % with respect to 2.0 dS /m, and 
electroconductivity about 4.8 dS/m reduced yield by an additional 50 % [22]. Additionally, there are nutritional as well as industrial 
qualitative traits that are threatened  because of salinity [23]. High salt concentrations impose ionic stress, osmotic stress and 
other secondary stresses such as nutritional disorders and oxidative stress that causes cell injury and photosynthesis reduction. 
Food security is being compromised by the climate change, the salinization of the aquifers and the increasing food demand for a 
growing population. It has been estimated that the global demand for rice in 2025 will increase from the 480 million tons 2013 rice 
production [24] to 715 million tons of milled rice. Many efforts have been made by international rice institutes to obtain salt tolerant 
lines. Recently, molecular markers were identified in rice that are strongly linked with a specific chromosomal region named 
“Saltol” which confer salt tolerance by correcting K +/Na+ levels and excluding sodium from plants  in the Pokkali variety and the 
Saltol introgressed lines (i.e. FL478 and IR64-Saltol). This Saltol region along with other major QTLs of salt tolerance has a known 
position in the rice genome and can be followed through molecular markers. So, using classical breeding and molecular markers, 
the salt tolerance regions can be effectively introgressed into the elite European rice cultivars along with maintaining classical 
European rice traits to obtain new salt tolerant commercial lines with interest to the European rice-farming sector and rice-industry 
sector. This new lines will be successfully commercialized in the European Community. 
Climate change. Global temperature has increased over the last century, especially during the last 50 years (0.13 ° C / decade).  
This warming has been more intense in the European Mediterranean region [2], being the effects most evident in spring and 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  7 
summer, contrasting to what happens in northern Europe where most notable increases are detected in winter. Temperature 
increases on the Mediterranean coastline is greater than those observed in other regions of the same latitude. In addition, due to 
scarcer water availability and the rise in sea levels, there is a clear tendency toward salinization in the river deltas wher e rice is 
grown in Europe, notably in the plots close to the sea level [2]. Simulations of regional climate models (RCM), performed during 
the EC project PRUDENCE, indicate that in the Mediterranean area temperatures will likely continue increasing at a faster rate 
than the global and European average during this century, so that in a few decades this in crease may be very obvious [2]. The 
increase of temperatures together with the rise of the sea level and the freshwater availability reduction are very likely to increase 
salinity levels especially in Mediterranean deltaic areas where rice is grown. Consequently, if measures are not taken before, the 
European rice production will greatly decrease. Having salt tolerant rice lines adapted to the environment that climate change is 
producing in the main European deltaic areas is an urgent objective for the European Community, and one of the main objective 
of the NEURICE project. 
The apple snail plague. The Apple snail species from genus Pomacea, including Pomacea insularum (described by d’Orbigny 
in 1835), are native of the South America wetlands. They have been widely introduced in Asia and Central and North America to 
be used as aquarium pets or human food [9, 10, 17-19]. The apple snail creates ecologic imbalances and destroys rice paddy 
fields, eating the sown seed and the rice plantlets, although they also feed on other plants [25]. These snails represent one of 
the worst gastropod crop pests of the recent times [5-10]. The Apple snail species are considered important exotic invasive 
species due to several characteristics they possess [18, 26]. In favourable conditions, they have a lifespan of 4 years [27], reach 
maturity in 2-4 months [28] and each female can lay about 8500-9000 eggs per season [29]. They are highly adaptable to harsh 
environmental conditions such as low dissolved O2 concentration, low food availability and low temperatures [9]. It is calculated 
that this plague has currently caused a damage equivalent to the loss of tens of billions of Euros in rice fields worldwide each 
year [11]. Recently, this harmful species, apple snails, entered accidentally the Ebro river delta. The Ebro delta in North East 
Spain is one of the finest wetlands in the western Mediterranean and plays a vital role in the local community while also serving 
as a stopover site for many migrant birds. This invasion represents a serious t hreat to Europe’s wetlands as it is spreading 
quickly. If the apple snail establishes itself across Europe, the consequences will be devastating for both Europe’s wetlands  
biodiversity and for rice European production. An evaluation of European Food Securi ty Authority (EFSA) at the end of 2013 
included Italy (the Po valley, which is the main rice production area in Europe) as an important hub for apple snail dispersal and 
epidemics. To date, the measures adopted to combat the apple snail and stop its spread have failed but, in the autumn of 2013, 
a new strategy was explored with permission of the European Union. This strategy was to flood 2500 ha of infested fields with 
seawater in advance of the 2014 growing season. The sea water treatment proved 100% effec tive in destroying apple snail 
infestations [12], however, the residual salinity caused a loss of productivity of about 30% in some fields [20]. If Europe had salt 
tolerant lines, with genes introgressed from FL478 or IR64-Saltol, problems arising from such management interventions could 
be avoided, and in this way, the natural environment of European rice producing regions could be maintained along with local 
rice genotypes. 
Remote Salinity Monitoring. As seawater treatment of rice fields is one of the most effective methods for apple snail control, it 
is very important to control and know accurately the level of salt, measured through electric conductivity, in the fields. Moreover, 
the climate change effects will increase the abiotic pressure on coastal and estuary areas in Europe and thus will raise the 
importance of knowing the levels of salinity in those areas in real time. This will increase, in return, the use of salty water for field 
rinsing and the effect of climate change and pest control on water scarcity. Agriculture is by far the biggest consumer of water 
and rice is more water consuming than many other crops: in continuous flooding cultivation, it takes about six times the water 
required by wheat. In fact, rice production consumes about 30 % of all freshwater used worldwide and production is challenged 
by the increasing shortage of water resource in the world and by the limitation of wat er resource in the seasonal drought areas 
[30]. For this reason, the project is proposing the development of a Wireless Sensor Network (WSN) for monitoring salinity in rice 
paddies in real time, prov iding the farmer a most valuable tool for improving the agricultural practices and the management of 
their fields while reducing environmental impact. Within this WSN, a decision support system will be developed to tailor the 
system to the needs of the agricultural community aiming at introducing smart-agriculture tools in the everyday management of 
fields. 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.

Taking into consideration these concepts, the objectives of the NEURICE project are: (i) to identify and introgress salt tolerant genes from salt-tolerant varieties to European elite rice cultivars 
and (ii) to develop a wireless salinity sensor monitoring in order to be prepared for the forthcoming climate change and to combat the apple snail plague, which could decrease the production 
of the main producing Mediterranean rice regions (Fig. 1).

NEURICE 
 1.3.2 Positioning of the project (from “idea to application”) 
Since the main pillar of the call is related to Sustainable Food Security, we have designed the proposal in order to prepare 
the European rice sector to respond to the growing threats: abiotic and biotic stresses (i.e. salinity and apple snail infest ation). 
The proposal is focused to achieve within 4 years: i) salt tolerant European rice varieties ready for registration, commercialization 
and distribution; ii) advanced salinity monitoring systems and iii) study of new rice salt tolerance alleles for mid -term further 
improvement of the obtained varieties. 
The European salt tolerant lines produced in this project will be registered and commercialized by NEURICE partners (CAMARA, 
CFR, CRA  and SIS) to ensure lab to market positioning . We plan to develop a collaborative, interdiscipl inary area for 
stakeholder engagement and knowledge sharing of common issues and drivers that present challenges to adaptive management.  
 
This project will bring together experts in diverse fields such as plant breeding (CIRAD, CFR, CRA, CAMARA), biotechnology 
(UB, CRAG, CIRAD, CRA, UMIL, UGLA, INDEAR and CAAS), plant physiology (UB, UGLA, IRTA and UMIL), farming and 
agriculture development (IRTA, CAMARA, CFR, CRA and SIS ), electrophysiology and cell signalling (UGLA) and sal inity 
monitoring systems (IRIS). This joint will foster new opportunities for training and additional collaborative research. Furthermore, 
the project is an ‘early development’ project that has the capacity to move quickly to ‘premarket’ development and therefore offers 
substantial promise for agroindustrial stakeholders. 
Furthermore, the results co-produced in the NEURICE project will be broadly transmitted and disseminated to the rice farmers 
sector in the form of seminars and field demonstrations by research centers, IRTA (Spain), CIR AD (France) and CRA (Italy). 
These work sessions will allow farmers to better know how to use the new salt-tolerant varieties, as well as how salinity control 
will be monitorized by the systems created by IRIS that will ensure a better adoption of NEURICE project results.

ii) A wireless sensors for salinity monitoring

 1.3.3 National and international research and innovation activities of partners 
Partners in volved in th is pro posal ha ve pa rticipated and/ or led national and/or i nternational research pr ojects, a nd 
therefore have the expertise and collected data that will be used to successfully achieve the aims of this proposal (Fig. 
2). 
 UB (PI Salvador Nogués) has participated in the COST project SIBAE ‘Stable isotopes in biosphere-atmosphere-earth 
system research (ES0806, 2009 -2012, 22 partners). UB, INDEAR are participating in the FP7 -KBBE-2011-5 project 
OPTIMA ‘Optimization of perennial grasses for biomass production in the Mediterranean environment (2011 -2015, 21 
partners), which is an inte rnational interdisciplinary project involving physiology, biotechnology, agronomy, socio -
economical and environmental analysis focused on important species of perennial grasses. 
 CRAG (PI Blanca San Segundo) is a public consortium that comprises research gr oups from the Spanish Research 
Council (CSIC), the Institute for Food and Agricultural Research and Technology (IRTA), the Autonomous University of 
Barcelona (UAB) and the University of Barcelona (UB). Areas of research at CRAG focus on the study of charac ters of 
interest in plants and farm animal species.  CRAG coordinated the ERA-Plant Genomics Project “Trilateral Initiative for 
Enhancing Salt Tolerance in Rice” (TRIESTER, ref. ERAPGFP/06.018B, 2007 -2010) in which 9 partners from Spain, 
France and Germany participated. Currently, CRAG and CRA are partners in the FACCE-JPI project on Climate Smart 
Agriculture ERA Net+ “Sustainable and Environmental friendly rice cultivation systems in Europe” -GreenRice that is 
coordinated by CIRAD (2014 -2017; 7 partners). C RAG was also Partner in the EURICE project (European Rice: 
transgenes for crop protection against fungal diseases (QLK5-1999-01484; 2000-2003), and together with IRTA, in the 
ERRI project (Engineering Rice for Insect Resistance; FAIR CT 97 -3761. BSS has been responsible for 13 Research 
Projects funded by the Spanish Ministry of Science and Innovation focusing on the molecular/cellular mechanisms and 
signalling networks governing the plant response to biotic and abiotic stress in plants (mainly, rice). 
 CIRAD (PI Brigitte Courtois) and CRA were partners in the EU funded projects RESGEN (1999-2002) and EURIGEN 
(2007-2010) that contributed to a better characterization of the European rice genetic resources, notably in terms of 
salinity tolerance and the developm ent of an associated database 
(http://eurigendb.cirad.fr/eurigen_home/JSP/index.jsp).  
 CRA (PI Giampiero Valè) coordinated two national research projects, RESPAT and RISINNOVA. RESPAT is a project 
dedicated to genomics of plant pathogens interactions funded by the Italian Agriculture Research Council and the Italian 
Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry ( MiPAF) (2009 -2011; 10 partners), while RISINNOVA is  a project dedicated to

 1.3.4 The overall approach and methodology 
An evaluation of germplasm to identify new salt tolerant accessions and a lleles will be carried out. For this evaluation, 
phenotypical selection, physiological analysis, Genome Wide Association Studies (GWAS) and allele mining wi ll be conducted 
on a germplasm collection of 300  japonica rice varieties and an available bi -parental population of 200 F6 RILs segregating for 
salt tolerance. This information will serve as a base for the results obtained in all the work packages. In parallel, a recently obtained 
high salinity tolerant variety called FL478 (IR29-Pokkali) will be used to introgress its salt tolerance chromosomal region into elite 
European cultivars (Fig. 3). FL478 is an advanced high-yielding and short cycle indica variety from the International Rice Research 
Institute (IRRI) introgressed with the Saltol salt tolerance chromosom al region from the well -known salt tolerant Pokkali Indian 
variety, so the crosses between FL478 and the European lines will produce high -yielding and salt tolerant varieties adapted to 
the European climate and market. Moreover, to fasten the crosses and breeding process, a molecular marker assisted 
backcrossing (MABC) selection technique will be coupled to an embryo rescue technique adaptation, which will allow us to obtain 
European varieties introgressed with Saltol region in just two years. To ensure that the FL478 salt tolerance alleles are 
introgressed, from F1 onward, along with a high amount of European parental genetic background, 60 to 70 KASPar markers will 
be used for the selection of the heterozygous plants and for background selection of the recurrent parent genome . The BC3F1 
plants will be self-pollinated in order to obtain homozygous Saltol BC3F2 plants and select those lines with the best return toward 
the recurrent parent(s). A set of approximately 20 BC3F3 homozygous Saltol lines from each country will be evaluated through 
hydroponic assays in greenhouse conditions under experimentally controlled salinity (0mM NaCl and 100 mM NaCl) inclu ding 
salt tolerant and salt sensitive (European) parental lines as controls. Non-destructive phenotyping protocols (thermal imaging and 
chlorophyll fluorescence) will be used to validate salt tolerant lines.  
Moreover, the Saltol donor ( FL478) and the most promising salt tolerant line from each country will be assessed again in 
hydroponic assays under 4 different salinity levels (0mM, 50 mM, 100mM and 150 mM). Deeper analysis for different physiological 
traits will be used to quantify traits in relation to Na+ and K+ transport and redistribution to further characterize one of the most  
promising salt tolerant lines of each country to compare with FL478 data. These analysis are: Na+ compartimentation analysis by 
fluorescent laser scanning confocal microscopy of root tissue vacuoles (CoroNa+ staining), leaf chlorophyll content, assessment 
of membrane integrity through evaluation of electrolyte leakage, determination of major membrane sterols by GC/MS ICPOES 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  13 
and direct electrophysiological methods. In addition, biochemical markers of oxidative stress (glutathione and malondialdehyde 
levels) will be evaluated on selected salt tolerant lines to characterize salt stress response of the rice accessions. Finall y, the 
expression level of genes involved in the sulphur metabolism (i.e. SULTR genes) will be analysed along with the expression level 
of other genes known to be involved in the response to salt stress using RNAseq in one line selected from each country lines.  
Six advanced breeding lines from each country will be assayed in salinized and non-salinized fields in the years 2018 and 2019 
in Ebro, Po and Rhône river deltas. For both years, the procedure will be as following: BC3F4 rice lines selected from BC3F3, as 
well as two salt tolerant japonica rice cultivars/RILs accessions, validated in hydroponic assays, will be evaluated for salt tolerance 
and commercial potential in terms of quality, productivity and cultivability to ensure that the original recipient traits are maintained. 
Lines will be tested in the natural growing area of their European parents, in this way, Italian accessions will be tested in the Po 
river delta, Spanish lines in the Ebro river delta and French accessions in the Rhône river delta. Parental lines used to obtain the 
new backcrossed lines will be included in the field trials as controls. For each line, salt tolerance, quality, yield and industrial traits 
will be assessed. Moreover, salinity will be monitored using a Wireless Sensor Network, based on low cost electrical conductivity 
sensors and an autonomous power supply based on energy harvesting which will provide real time data of the salinity conditions 
of the rice paddies, developed within this project in both, Spanish and Italian fields. Productivity, quality and industrial traits will 
be evaluated in rice grains of the selected tolerant lines. A work plan to disseminate and transfers the results to the society,  
research centers and universities and the rice -farming sector will be implemented. Its objective will be guaranteeing the proper 
transfer of the results obtained in this project using a website, publications, posters, journal articles and seminars. Open field days 
will be performed in 2018 and 2019 to explain to rice farmers how the new varieties should be used, how the wireless sen sor 
network works, and how to deal with salinity in rice paddies whether it is due to the climate change effects or to the saltwa ter 
treatments to stop the apple snail pest. Moreover, at the end of the project, the end -users will benefit from the new salt tolerant 
lines registered by the competent partners in each country for its commercialization in the European community as well as other 
countries all over the world.

 1.3.5 Sex/gender issue 
Partners’ institutions have equal opportunity policies.  No sex or gender discrimination was u sed in the p articipants' 
selection. All personnel were enrolled only on the basis of their professional expertise and motivated personal interest to participate 
in the common European research. We are also unusually well balanced in terms of gender (ca. 45% are female participants), 
with women taking many of the leading roles. Among female participants, there are high quality experts:  
 Marta López-Carbonell and Teresa Sauras from University of Barcelona (P1, UB). 
 Blanca San Segundo leader (PI) from Center for Research in Agricultural Genomics (P2, CRAG). 
 Brigitte Courtois (PI) leader of the Agricultural Research for Development (P3, CIRAD). 
 Elena Baldoni from Università degli Studi di Milano (P5, UMIL)  
 Maria del Mar Català (PI) and Fanny Alvaro from Institut de Recerca i Tecnologia Agroalimentària (P7, IRTA).

 Roser Llaó Garcia and Mònica Reverté Calvet from la Cámara Arrocera del Montsià (P10, CAMARA).  
 
To promote gender-equality in terms of decision -making, three women are WP leaders. Thus, Brigitte Courtois is the leader of 
WP2 due to her expertise in rice breeding, Blanca San Segundo is the leader of WP3 due to her expertise in rice physiology and 
genomics, and finally Maria del Mar Català is the leader of WP6 due to her expertise in conducting field seminars to communicate 
and transfer knowledge and results to farmers. All partners will encourage application of female researchers when recruiting 
additional project personnel or students. The project itself is considered as gender neutral in terms of its research priorities and 
impact. 
 
 
 1.4. Ambition 
 1.4.1 Ambitions of NEURICE 
The main ambition of NEURICE is to develop  two new salt tolerant European elite varieties per each Mediterranean 
country involved in the project (Spain, France and Italy) to be commercialized in Europe. This will be done through a multi-actor 
approach for the protection of European rice production from emerging abiotic (salt stress due to climate change) and biotic 
(apple snail, which is controlled with seawater treatments ). These problems could pose serious losses in the European rice 
production (that has already decreased between 2013 and 2014).  
The project addresses the challenges of both abiotic and biotic stress threats, and does so taking advantage of the 
consequences of one to control the other. Climate change impacts on European rice threat to reduce yields as a consequence of 
paddy salinization. Introducing salt-tolerant alleles, including the major QTL region called Saltol recently discovered that confers 
a strong salt tolerance, into commercial elite European rice varieties will relieve the negative effects of salinization in rice cultivation 
and will greatly improve rice seed commerce and rice genotypes in Europe through the registration of these new salt tolerant elite 
European rice varieties. Consequently, these new varieties will help to grow rice where the salinity levels, due to climate change 
or natural salinization, have increased to high levels.  Moreover, these varieties will also permit to use the only effective method, 
seawater flooding of rice paddies, for eradicating apple snail infestations that are currently spreading through several major rice-
producing areas around the Mediterranean zone and that have proven to be a severe plague in Asia, Central and North America. 
Different projects are being developed to face the climate change effects on rice. Some of them face greenhouse gases emissions 
such as Ebro Admiclim (http://www.lifeebroadmiclim.eu/es/) LIFE project in Europe and GLOBAL RESEARCH ALLIANCE (Asia-
LatinAmerica consortium) projects ( http://www.globalresearchalliance.org/research/paddy-rice-research-group/). Other projects 
try to face  flooding problems caused by the climate  change, such as CLUES (http://irri.org/networks/climate-change-affecting-
land-use-in-the-mekong-delta) in Mekong delta. Others try to modify the management prac tices to reduce water consumption 
such as CLIMARICE ( http://www.climarice.org/) in India. Other projects are focused in avoiding salinity through interspecific 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  15 
hybridizations between Oryza sativa and O. glaberrima, such as STRASA in Africa ( http://strasa.irri.org/), while others try to 
discover new salt tolerant alleles in American rice varieties  
(http://www.ars.usda.gov/research/projects/projects.htm?accn_no=426485). 
Recently, a major QTL for salt tolerance has been found in Pokkali, an ancient rice variety from Kerala (India), which confers salt 
tolerance up to 150 mM NaCl. This revolutionary salt tolerance QTL called Saltol has been introgressed into IR29 line by IRRI to 
obtain FL478 (IR 66946-3R-178-1-1), that has been promoted as an improved donor for breeding programs, as it has a high level 
salinity tolerance and is photoperiod insensitive, shorter and flowers earlier than the original Pokkali landrace [33-35]. 
Introgression of the Saltol region from FL478 into other indica rice varieties has successfully produced new salt tolerant varieties 
in Vietnam [36, 37] and India [38], but no studies have been developed about Saltol introgressions in European temperate rice 
accessions or even in temperate japonica rice accessions in general. 
In this project, new salt tolerant temperate japonica rice accessions will be identified, and a GWAS analysis will be performed to 
determine loci involved in salt tolerance as well as an evaluation of allelic diversity in candidate salt tolerance genes through allele 
mining. Moreover, the methodologies proposed to obtain new varieties combine classical breeding assisted with molecular 
markers with a nd in vitro  embryo rescue technique  that permits germinating embryos 10 days after fertilization . Thus, 
performing these methodologies with different rice varieties from thr ee rice -producing countries in Europe will advance rice 
breeding programs and will lead rice research . In addition, it will broaden the knowledge needed to develop salt tolerance in  
temperate japonica rice varieties (the most produced and consumed rice  cultivars in Europe) since the current information is 
available only for indica and tropical japonica rice varieties.  In addition, phenotypical selection along with physiological, 
biochemical, genomic and transcriptomic assays and studies will be carried out through the project . This approach will expand 
knowledge on salt tolerance mechanis ms of rice at the physiological and molecular level , which are at this time still not fully 
understood, even though rice has been cultivated in Europe since the 8th century [39]. Some of these techniques are detailed 
Na+/K+ studies (transport, distribution and translocation), ROS measure ments and RNA sequencing. The knowledge obtained 
will serve to establish where new salt tolerant varieties should be used and which ones are best applied in new breeding programs. 
Finally, candidate salt tolerant lines will be tested in rice paddy fields to assess their commerciality within the European rice 
farming and industry sector. The field trials will be accompanied by a remote salinity monitoring system using a wireless sensor 
network. These remote salinity monitoring systems will be developed to alert rice farmers and the rice industry about the use of 
the salt tolerant varieties and will help avoid losses due to the salinity increase in the fields or to reduce the environmental impact 
of seawater flooding for pest control . To achieve these ambitious objectives, the NEURICE project relies on innovative 
breakthroughs in plant and pathogen biology fostered from (i) one side by the knowledge of the rice crop genome sequence for 
the identification and introduction of useful genetic variation and (ii) from other approaches for land management that will be 
applied. This project is also designed in order to develop ambitious and ground-breaking objectives such as the joint approach to 
salinity problems using new salt tolerant varieties with remote salinity monitoring systems in order to evaluate, control and respond 
to the complex interactions of specific management interventions. Moreover, the NEURICE consortium will ensure that the end-
users involved in this project (CFR, SIS,  CRA, CAMARA) will send new tolerant lines to registry and to make them available to 
the rice-industry and rice-farming sector. 
 
1.4.2 Innovation potential of NEURICE 
The NEURICE project will use a combination of Molecular marker assisted breeding and embryo rescue techniques 
to rapidly and efficiently obtain and commercialize salt tolerant European rice varieties. An efficient and rapid salt tolera nce 
introgression protocol adapted to local constraints will be developed for European rice accessions. The innovation aspect comes 
from the background in which the chromosome segment carrying the Saltol region QTL will be introgressed. Such transfer has 
not yet been attem pted in temperate japonica rice. The material produced will enable to validate the effect of the QTL coming 
from an indica rice background in a temperate japonica rice background and assess the extent of the possible QTL x g enetic 
background interactions. 
Presence of new loci conferring tolerance to mild salinity stress will be investigated within a germplasm panel of japonica rice 
through a GWAS approach and within a biparental RIL population through a linkage mapping approach. Non -destructive high-
throughput phenotyping procedures, conducted on paddy soil in controlled environment, will assess the two mapping procedures 
and candidate genes will be characterized by allele mining. The study will provide both information about salt tolerance loci in a 
japonica genetic background and led to the identification of japonica accessions bearing mild tolerance to salt stress. These 
activities will take advantage from the GreenRice Project’s work in which salt tolerance evaluations of germplasm collections will 
be carried out in hydroponic conditions. 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  16 
A challenge for the project will be to conduct the introgression program at the rate of three generations per year in order to have 
products usable in the framework of the project. To achieve this propose we will fasten M olecular marker assisted breeding by 
coupling it to embryo rescue technique that permits embryo germination 7 days after fertilization. This goal will allow to develop 
a  marker-aided backcross scheme enabling both to reduce the size of the introgressed se gment to the smallest possible size 
and ensuring an almost perfect return toward the recipient parent, and to accompany it by an excellent logistic. Once tested and 
validated by the three partners (CAMARA, CFR, SIS), this scheme could be used for similar introgression work using other genes.  
Furthermore, the methods to assess the salt tolerance of the material will use a combination of high throughput techniques (infra-
red imaging) at the plant level and advanced techniques looking at salt effect up to the cell level. Finally, innovative salt tolerance 
allele detection techniques will be used to identify new sources of salt tolerance alleles in japonica rice cultivars and monitor salt 
tolerance inheritance inbred lines.  
A high reliability remote salinity m onitoring systems, wireless sensor network,  will be developed for salt resistant field trials in 
order to control and improve the effects of salinity on the productivity of the rice fields. Through the development of a low -cost 
monitoring system it will be possible to control large rice areas while obtaining accurate local data of salinity, and thus of the effect 
of the proposed water management interventions. The innovation of this wireless sensor network will help give the rice sector key 
feedback for management practices by allowing to evaluate the environmental changes in regards to salinity, and thus use the 
new salt tolerant varieties to mitigate its damage. 
Currently, there are no European rice varieties available for European farmers with sufficient salt tolerance to face salinity 
problems. Thus, the project will produce advanced breeding lines with a high level of salinity tolerance in locally adapted genetic 
backgrounds and to test their adaptation in a range of environments. The best one(s) of thes e new lines will be selected to be 
later registered and commercialized as cultivar(s), increasing the basket of varieties available for farmers. Among the partn ers, 
there are institutions which are conducting conventional breeding programs for the target a rea (CAMARA, CFR,CRA and SIS) 
and who are the best at testing relevant traits of the cultivars, and ensuring a fast transmission of the advanced material t o the 
farmers.

programme and the impacts defined in this topic description (Table 2.1.a.).

varieties will protect the rice sector from productivity loses due to salinity levels derived from 
the climate change and from treating fields with seawater to stop the apple snail infestation. 
The know-how of growing these new varieties will be fed into the EU end -users (CAMARA,

The new salt tolerant elite European rice varieties wi ll be obtained with a novel 
breeding strategy, that includes molecular marker assisted breeding coupled with embry o 
rescue on immature seeds. It will be entirely developed within the NEURICE project, i.e. the 
introgression of salt tolerance into elite European varieties using the most salt resistance 
alleles from resistant rice lines such as Pokkali, FL478 and IR64-Saltol. It has been reported 
that Pokkali and FL478 can grow up to 150mM NaCl concentrations, while the most salt 
tolerant European cultivars just can tolerate salinity ranges between 30 and 60 mM. This 
development will broaden the knowledge on salinity tole rance alleles and will therefore 
support productivity and stability of the agricultural sector in Europe and possibly beyond.

management strategies 
which allow for increased 
diversity and show higher 
adaptability to particular 
environments including 
under a changing climate. 
The new improved salt tolerant varieties will allow maintaining the natural 
environment of the rice growing regions as well as increasing rice diversity for a higher 
adaptability to particular environments, including abiotic and biotic stresses tolerance to face 
a changing climate scenario. In addition, the apple snail dispersion throughout Europe can 
be stopped or even eradicated thanks to the availability of these new salt tolerant European 
varieties, as se awater treatments of infested fields (that proved 100% efficacy) can be 
resumed, avoiding less effective and highly contaminant chemical strategies. 
Over a longer term, 
knowledge and tools created 
shall support productivity 
and stability of the 
agricultural sector in Europe 
and possible beyond. 
The consortium of the NEURICE project involves Spain, France and Italy, which are 
accounted for an 83% of the European rice production, thus this project will contribute to 
reinforce the position of the EU in the fi eld of plant health and cereal production, 
attractiveness of research European centres in plant sciences and innovation in the 
European rice sector. Moreover, this project addresses a common societal challenge of vital 
concern on food safety, by providing control strategies against the imminent climate change 
and a possible pest of rice that is known to cause huge yield losses. The WSN system 
developed within NEURICE intends to become part of the tools used in agricultural practises 
and field management in order to improve the productivity of agriculture in Europe, but also 
in all areas where salinity is a problem or a potential threat due to climate change.

NEURICE  18 
Other impacts (not explicitly listed in the call):   
Along with developing new salt tolerant varieties, a wireless salinity monitoring sensor network will be developed by IRIS, which 
will alert the rice farmers and cooperatives of salinity increments so they can shift to grow the salt tolerant varieties developed in 
the project. 
Identification of mild s alt stress tolerant loci and accessions in japonica background through utilization of mapping approaches 
coupled with non-destructive phenotyping will permit advancing in rice salt tolerance knowledge and, as a consequence, will 
permit introgress other additive salt tolerant loci to the European advanced Saltol lines to further increase the rice salt tolerance 
in future rice breeding programs. 
The multi -actor approach of the NEURICE project will strengthen research and innovation collaboration between Europ e, 
Argentina and People’s Republic of China in line with priorities identified under existing policy dialogues and related projects and 
initiatives. In addition, it will improve the innovation capacity and growth of companies by developing new products such new salt 
tolerant varieties and salinity monitoring systems, which meet the needs of European markets. NEURICE involves end -users, 
CAMARA, CFR, CRA and SIS, which will commercialize these new varieties and will be prepared to face problems due to climate 
change perturbations and/or apple snail plague so that the EU rice sector maintains their productivity and stability. 
Moreover, the NEURICE project will support the development of an innovative ecosystem in the agrifood sector in the EU  and 
the development of the European Innovation Partnership on productive and sustainable agriculture (EIP -AGRI). The agrifood 
sector needs to answer the societal and consumer demand for safe, healthy and sustainable food, while continuing to export (i.e. 
the rice exports were maintained at 212,000 t in 2014) and compete in international markets providing jobs for more than 4 million 
people across Europe. The EU has about 14 million farmers with a further 4 million people working in the food sector. The farming 
and food sectors together provide 7% of all jobs and generate 6% of European gross domestic product. The agrifood sector in 
the EU plays a central role for its economic importance and also for its social and environmental implications. 
At the same time, there are wide v ariations within the agricultural sector in the EU that must be considered. The structure and 
characteristics of this sector can be very different, with different actors assuming distinct roles and having different w eights 
according to the country (i.e. farmers, farmer associations, SMEs, research centres).  The EU recognises the need to promote 
cooperation amongst the different actors of this sector, but especially between the “producers” of science a nd technology and 
end-users.  
There is therefore a need f or strategies that generate the necessary confidence among innovation actors and to link them 
effectively, as well as to integrate the needs from end users (farmers, coop eratives, SME´s) in the innovation chain. This will 
contribute to align the development of innovative products and services to the existing supply of knowledge and technology from 
research centres and universities.  The NEURICE project will provide good practices  and recommendations adapted to the 
different EU countries, to help them in the development of this innovative sector.
2.2 Measures to maximise impact 
 
2.2.1. Dissemination and exploitation of results  
When constructing NEURICE work -plan, particular attention has been paid to actions that can adequately support an 
integrated knowledge, a dissemination strategy and an effective exploitation of the project results. For this, the NEURICE project 
has prepared several activities oriented towards results dissemination to general and scientific public. Moreover, we need to  
ensure salt tolerant rice lines registration and commercialization at the industrial level as well as of the wireless sensor network, 
while complementing with activities specifically orientated to the seed industry, European rice sector companies and European  
rice cooperatives and farmers in order to show the new lines growing in paddies and ensure the knowledge transfer (WP6). 
NEURICE project will launch and maintain a website to ensure proper dissemination and transfer of the ongoing development of 
the different work packages and to serve as a platform for researchers and rice seed industries interested in the project to contact 
any of the partners involved. Project leaflets, posters, presentations as well as publications in periodic press releases in local, 
regional, national, and international newspapers will be done. Partners also have a commitment to publish the breakthrough 
results obtained in this project to ensure its transfer and availability to researchers in Europe and all over the world. 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  19 
In order to support the elite European salt tolerant rice lines (final product) commercialization, and to support availability for the 
seed industry and rice farmers, rice farmer associations and cooperatives are involved in open field days demonstrations to rice 
farmers. These open field days will be performed in Rhône delta (CFR), Po delta (CRA) and Ebro delta (IRTA), which will include 
seminars and field demonstrations to show the new lines. Furthermore, in order to support wireless sensor network to monitor 
salinity (final product), IRIS will be accompanied by CFR, CRA and IRTA in the previously mentioned open field days in Rhône 
delta (CFR), Po delta (CRA) and Ebro delta (IRTA). IRIS will conduct seminars to  explain the application of the wireless sensor 
network to monitor salinity to know when there will be need to use these new elite European salt tolerant lines.  
These activities will ensure knowledge transfer and exploitation of the results obtained in the NEURICE project. 
The Communication and Dissemination plan will also define a model and the mechanisms for engaging the agricultural European 
Innovation Partnership (EIP -AGRI) Service Point and the different EIP national/regional networks in the project, including the 
connection with EIP databases. The main goal is to use the NEURICE outcomes, activities and material to feed the EIP website 
and update and maintain their database. This model will include: 
 The identification of different relevant players at EU and national /regional levels; 
 The definition of protocols and standards to ensure the embedment with the existing EIP networks (EU EIP network 
and the different national EIP networks that will be created in the EU Member States, following RDP 
recommendations); 
 Development of the framework for the participation of interested institutions and co-ownership of the system. 
 
Initial business and exploitation plans  
Over the course of the project we will develop new rice varieties with salt resistance and a wireless sensor network with a decision 
support system for improved agricultural practises. The project outputs are highly relevant for future market exploitation. Critically, 
all the expected impacts from this project that have been discussed in Section 2.1 can only be realised through a robust post -
project exploitation strategy. Our intention is to realise all the exploitation pathways for the results:  
a) Commercial exploitation- the industrial use of the project knowledge and outputs for increased competitiveness and 
growth will deliver high innovation and growth impacts;  
b) Education and training- the use of the new knowledge generated for upskilling and for enriching curricula in European 
education will have a high impact for raise the European rice and agriculture knowledge base;  
c) Further research- planning future spin-out research and development projects especially in areas that will contribute to 
the transferability of the project results to new applications;  
d) Contribution to standards- the project results can contribute to rice variety breeding standards for example.  
 
Each partner has communicated clear exploitation expectations (table 2.2.1.a), which will be planned in greater detail during Task
6.3 Knowledge transfer and exploitation of results. Importantly, a first exploitation/business plan has been drawn up considering 
the contribution of the results to patents, to new or existing products, services, infrastructures, knowledge bases and stand ards, 
to ensure the project innovations are delivered to the market.

How the proposed measures will help to achieve the expected impact of the project 
Fundamental to achieving the expected impacts of this project, is to enable SMEs to enter the research-development-innovation 
cycle of crop productivity and farm management and to ensure the project effort takes industry closer to bringing new technologies, 
processes and products onto the market to benefit society and the environment and to lead to growth and value added jobs in 
Europe. To realise these goals, there is a strong innovation dimension/cycle in the project approach with a view to increasing 
the likelihood of continuity of the established ecosystem, as well as market uptake of project results for European 
agricultural sustainability, competitiveness, growth, and jobs.  
Strong industry and academia involvement in the consortium, backed by robust knowledge management, knowledge transfer 
and market exploitation plans, will contribute to ensuring that the NEURICE project is successful in transitioning knowledge 
towards the market. A key measure for contributing to industry adoption of research results lies in a R&D offering that is founded 
on the agricultural industry requirements. It is noteworthy that the NEURICE work plan is based on a rising problem for the r ice 
sector across Europe, which  has a potential for severely affecting agricultural productivity. To this end, the R&D w ork is 
implemented with industry, market, regulatory and end user considerations and constraints in mind.  
It is noteworthy that this consortium is led by UB, who has vast experience in leading European R&D projects, and counts with 4 
SMEs which have already been part of research projects and that are geared towards market-oriented exploitation. Linking 
industry with the right RTOs is vital for success. To this end, the involvement of RTOs of international renown in the fields  of 
breeding (CIRAD, CFR, CRA, CAMARA), biotechnology (UGLA, UB, CRAG, UMIL, CRA, INDEAR and CAAS), plant physiology 
(UB, UGLA, IRTA, UMIL and CRA), farming and agriculture development (IRTA, CAMARA, CFR and UMIL), electrophysiology 
and cell signalling (UGLA) and salinity monitoring systems (IRIS), thereby fostering new opportunities for training and additional 
collaborative research. This ‘early development’ project has the capacity to move quickly to ‘premarket’ development and therefore 
offers substantial promise for agroindustrial stakeholders.  These will help in transferring research results to industry, as well as 
providing training and educational programmes, added value assets, which when combined with industry drive will ensure we 
bridge the innovation gap that frequently prevents industry adoption the results and R&D outputs. 
While the involvement of industry in R&D consortia increases the success rate of market -oriented exploitation , vertical 
integration (i.e. including the whole value chain)  in R&D projects is a success factor  for market-oriented exploitation. The 
consortium counts a synergistic mix of technology SME companies (IRIS) and agricultural SMEs (CAMARA, CFR, SIS) which are 
committed to routing project outputs to market. Moreover, SIS as an international seed company will act as end user enlarging 
the direct market uptake of the project results. They all have the in-house R&D capacity to perform further advancements of the 
TRLs to achieve a minimum level of vali dation and commercial viability. They  will pave the way fo rward for a timely 
commercialisation phase to see the upgraded agricultural practises and productivity being swiftly used towards full products and 
market adoption of the NEURICE solutions within 2 years of project completion. They will also contribute to technology push as 
they are not only charged to contribute to the R&D effort, especially in the context of scale-up, integration and demonstration 
of the results during the project ,  but can absorb the knowledge generated, in order to quickly commercialise the project 
outputs. This way they can serve strong industry demand that will be stimulated because of the market pull generated by the 
participating end-users (SIS), as well as other in the agricultural industry, end -users of salt resistant plant varieti es, and smart 
agriculture companies. Importantly , the inclusion of partners that are experts in supporting farmers and ensuring stability and 
productivity of agriculture (IRTA, CRA) and in market uptake ( CAMARA, SIS) is an important added value for the con sortium. 
Furthermore, they will contribute to ensuring a systematic and methodological approach to planning for the important post-project 
exploitation stage is in place from the project outset to ensure success.   
Ensuring that measures are in place to id entify and study the impacts of relevant rice varieties aspects, regulations and the 
requirements of industry standards will contribute to ensuring that are no market obstacles could prevent the future commerci al 
adoption of the NEURICE  technologies post project. In addition, the validation (field trials WP 4) will include productivity 
assessments, as well as salt tolerance tests for ensuring a wide use across different salinity stress conditions, as well as 
confirming its cost competitiveness and its environmental benefits. Furthermore, the results will provide invaluable data for helping 
to push the results to the market, and at the same time stimulating market pull.

As seed breeding, rice growing and remote field condition monitoring cover highly multidisciplinary fields, there is a high doorstep 
for smaller companies and farmers. To overcome this, different points are needed for raising technical skills and the knowledge 
base among the rice farming, seed breeding and agriculture technology industry: 
 Structured knowledge transfer and training effort towards the industry on the use of newly developed rice varieties with 
induced salt resistance. 
 The wireless sensor network use for agricultural management. 
 The competitive and wider socio-economic benefits of enhanced agricultural production through research, and standards 
and regulations.  
This way we can ensure they are prepared for management decisions in relation to the investments in novel breeding lines and 
new technology deployment. This will be shown through the training activities organised in Task 6.3 Knowledge transfer and 
exploitation of results, as well as through the exploitation route of using the project knowledge for future training and education 
programmes by IRTA.  
Other aspects will also increase the likelihood of market uptake of the project results: 
 Sound management of the knowledge generated during the project. 
 Active planning in relation to post-project exploitation activities for industrialisation of the most market ready results. 
 Further research work for escalating along the TRLs, or indeed for application of the platform knowledge generated 
during this project beyond the rice industry (other cereals, fruit and vegetables). 
 A solid communication strategy to disseminate the non-confidential aspects of the result to the European sectors related 
to the project EIP -AGRI, SFS, PRIMA community and beyond, as well as to market actors and multipliers,  and policy 
makers. 
As an example, the results obtained in the NEURICE project will be transmitted to the rice farmers sector in the form of seminars 
and field demonstrations by the research centers, IRTA (Spain), CIRAD (France) and CRA (Italy). These work sessions will 
explain to farmers how to use the new varieties, as well as how salinity levels can be monitorized by the systems created in the 
NEURICE project. 
The business plans that will be drawn up during Task 6.3 Knowledge transfer and exploitation of results, building on the preliminary 
exploitation plans outlined in this document, will provide the details on how the project’s results will be used in commercial 
exploitation activities, for training purposes, for further research activities as well as for standardisation activities.  
In short, all the ingredients are present to achieve the expected impact of the project-sound innovation measures and a relevant 
value chain of actors in the consortium who are in pursuit of a common goal. 
How the participants will manage the research data generated and/or collected during the project 
The NEURICE project will not participate in the Pilot Open Access Research Data scheme, and all the research data generated 
by the project will be used for the purposes of the development of the project results.

To pave the way forward for commercial exploitation and dissemination of the project results, the consortium will implement an 
integral strategy for the effective management of this knowledge  based on the IPR definition and dissemination of non -
confidential results.

Results definition, protection, ownership and access rights  
 
The expected results from the project are listed in Table 2.2.1.c. below, and will be continually assessed in terms of novelty, 
patentability and protection as part of Task 6.3 Knowledge transfer and exploitation of results, sub-task 6.3.1. Protection of the 
IPR, as part of an effective knowledge management strategy.  Results shall be owned by the participant generating them. To 
avoid doubt or confusion over ownership, a protocol of procedures will be defined, which will be followed by each partner to clearly 
show the development of the generation of knowledge or results. In cases where the results are generated jointly (i.e. where the 
separate parts of some result cannot be attributed to different participants), it will be jointly owned. The allocation and the terms 
of exercising this joint ownership will be agreed in Joint Ownership Agreements that will be established during Task 6.3 Knowledge 
transfer and exploitation of results, sub-task 6.3.2. IPR Ownership and Sharing. Access rights to results if needed for implementing 
the project will be granted on a royalty -free basis. Access rights for use purposes will be granted either royalty-free, or on fair 
and reasonable conditions  to be agreed in the NEURICE Exploitation Agreement. Table 2.2.c provides an overview  of the

Open access to peer-reviewed scientific publications  
 
The two ways authors can provide open access are: 
 By self-archiving their journal articles in an open access repository, also known as 'green' open access 
 By publishing in an open access journal, known as 'gold' open access[40].  
It is envisaged that green open access will be the preferred option in this project, whereby the partners will publish in peer -
reviewed scientific publications and then self-archive a version of the article for free public use in their institutional repository, in 
a central repository, or on some other open access website. The project website (or Internet Portal) will house a ‘NEURICE Green 
Channel’ for open access to the peer -reviewed publications of the project. In relation to expected publications from the project, 
these include and are not limited to: plant physiology, plant breeding, plant transcriptomics, oxidative stress, agricultural novelties, 
resource management,  etc. The University of Barcelona (UB), coordinator of NEURICE, has an institutional repository 
(http://diposit.ub.edu) publicly accessible to anyone, with several collections , among them one dedicated to research outputs 
(http://hdl.handle.net/2445/7181). Any researcher can upload a copy of any reviewed published paper through the Current 
Research Information System (CRIS) avail able at the institution. Researchers are informed of the self -archiving policies of the 
publication and they are asked to deliver a copy of the document in the suitable version: final publication, postprint or preprint. All 
rights metadata and possible emb argoes are automatically introduced in the system. If there is a requirement for an embargo 
period, all the metadata of the publication are publicly available at the repository but the document is locked until the specific date. 
The institutional repository of the UB meets all the requirements for OAI-PMH harvesting and therefore it is acknowledged as an 
OpenAIRE compliant repository.
