3. Implementation
3.1 Work plan — Work packages, deliverables and milestones  
 To ensure a proper development of the NEURICE project and to meet all the objectives proposed, its w ork plan has 
been divided into seven work packages whose description and organization (Fig. 4) is shown below: 
 
 
 
WP1: Germplasm evaluation and genetic mapping for salt tolerance.  
 
  Analyses will be conducted on: i) FL478 and IR64-Saltol, the salt tolerance donors that will be used in WP2, ii) 
a germplasm collection of 300 japonica rice varieties and iii) an available bi -parental population of 200 F6 RILs 
segregating for salt tolerance. Phenotyping will be conducted in greenhouse for two years on pots filled with submerged 
soils with a mid-level (around 5dS/m) of salinity controlled by conductivity (UMIL). Different parameters will be evaluated: 
i) comparison of germination rate in saline and non -saline soil; ii) plants growth curve and leaf damages evalua tion 
monitored at different phenological stages by semi-automated photo cameras and dedicated software system; iii) thermal 
imaging at different phenological stages using long-wave infrared cameras; iv) spikelet sterility. Furthermore, a one-year 
phenotyping of a stronger salt treatment using a submerged soil with an electrical conductivity around 10 dS/m will be 
conducted, using a core collection expressly generated. For this purpose, after the first year of phenotyping, the 
germplasm will be divided in cl usters, depending on the tolerance level to salt treatment. The tolerance data will be 
compared with genotypic data (molecular markers) to extract a core collection of a few genotypes, representative of the 
entire variability for salt tolerance in the whole germplasm collection. 
The 200 RILs population will be genotyped using Genotyping By Sequencing (GBS) by INDEAR. The identification of 
loci involved in mid salt tolerance will be conducted in the 300 accessions germplasm collection, already genotyped 
using GBS, and the 200 RILs population by CRA and INDEAR respectively through a GWAS and a linkage mapping 
approaches. For both mapping approaches, bioinformatics analyses will be carried out for the identification of candidate 
genes underlying the phenotypic effect of mid salt tolerance and alleles re -sequencing in tolerant and susceptible 
accessions will be conducted for suitable candidates (CAAS, INDEAR, CRA, UMIL). In addition, an in-depth physiological 
study using 4 conditions of salinity on hydroponic cul ture (0, 50, 100 and 150 mM) will be carried out on the highly salt 
tolerant line FL478 (UB, UGLA). 
 
 
WP2: Salt tolerance introgression  from salt tolerant varieties into 6 elite European cultivars, 2 from each country 
involved: Spain, Italy and France.  
  A molecular marker assisted back -crossing (MABC) breeding coupled to an embryo rescue (ER) technique 
adaptation will be applied to an already available collection of F1 lines obtained by crossing Saltol rice varieties (IR64-
Saltol and FL478) with elite European rice accessions. This approach will yield Saltol salt tolerant accessions with elite 
European varieties background in just two years. The marker assisted back-cross (MABC) program will be conducted to 
transfer the Saltol and QTL regions into 2 elite lines from Spain, 2 from Italy and 2 from France (UB, CRAG, CIRAD, 
CRA and CFR). From F1 onward, a set of 60-70 KASPar markers will be used to asses that the Saltol region is present 
in the carrier chromosome as well as to determine which plants have the best return toward the recurrent parent. This 
strategy will allow for selecting the best beachhead plants as starting points of the program. The number of BC1F1 plants 
will be large but the number of plants genotyped at each BC generation will decrease with  the advance of the project. 
From the BC3 generation, part of the BC3F1 plants will be self -pollinated and the BC3F2 plants with the smallest 
introgressed segment at the homozygous state and good return toward the recipient parent will be selected and BC3F3 
seeds used for a first phenotypic evaluation under controlled hydroponic conditions. 
 
WP3: Salt tolerance validation and mechanisms study.  
  The European lines obtained in the WP2 will be validated using hydroponic assays at 0mM and 100 mM NaCl 
(CRAG, CIRAD, CRA). BC3F3 seeds from twenty BC3F2 homozygous Saltol lines from each Spanish, French and Italian 
elite varieties will be assessed in greenhouse conditions under no salinity (0 mM NCl) and experimentally controlled high 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  28 
salinity (100 mM NaCl) including salt tolerant (FL478 salt tolerance donor) and salt sensitive elite (European) parentals 
as crosschecks. The non-destructive phenotyping protocols used in WP1 (thermal imaging and chlorophyll fluorescence) 
will used in this WP for the validation of salt tolerant lines. The six most salt tolerant lines of each country will be selected 
for WP4 field trials. Moreover, the most promising salt tolerant lines, one from each country,  as well as six selected 
japonica rice cultivars/RILs accessions (two sensitive , two tolerant and two with an intermediate tolerant phenotype), 
derived from WP1 activities,  will be analysed in detail in hydroponic conditions performed by CRAG at 0, 50, 100 and 
150 mM NaCl. In addition, biochemical markers of oxidative stress will be evaluated to characterize salt stress response 
of the rice accessions, such as: differences in GSH levels (UMIL) and malondialdehyde (MDA) levels (UB). Finally, the 
expression level of genes involved in the sulphur metabolism as well as the expression level of other genes known to be 
involved in the response to salt stress will be evaluated by UMIL  and RNA sequencing will be carried out by CRAG to 
selected lines of all countries comparing lines cultivated at 0 and 50 mM NaCl.  
 
WP4: Field assays of the adv anced breeding lines in the summer of the years 2018 (mid -scale assay) and 2019 
(large-scale assay).  
  To ensure a proper evaluation of the lines a multi -actor approach will be used that consists in that each new 
produced line will be evaluated in the reg ions of their parental rice lines in the field of the e nd-users of the NEURICE 
project. For both years, the procedure will be as following: 6 BC3F4 lines from each Spanish, Italian and French elite 
lines (a total of 18 lines) , as well as two salt tolerant japonica rice cultivars/RILs accessions, selected in WP3 will be 
assayed in salinized and non-salinized fields. Lines will be tested in the natural growing area of their European parents, 
in this way, Italian accessions will be tested in the Po river delta, Spanish lines in Ebro river delta and French accessions 
Rhône river delta (CFR). The parental lines used to obtain those BC3F4 lines will be included in this assays in order to 
be able to compare and select those BC3F4 lines with commercial potential in terms of quality, productivity and 
cultivability to ensure that the original recipient traits are maintained, and the lines are effectively salt tolerant. Standard 
fertilization and field management principles of each growing area (country) will be applied. The experimental design will 
be the same in non -salinized and in fields destined to salinity tolerance assays  (split-plot with 4 replications); IRIS will 
monitor salinity using a Wireless Sensor Network for salinity in salinized and non -salinized trials in Spain, Italy and 
France. At least eight plants will be randomly selected from each line in order to record data measurements. General 
agronomic, production and quality of plants as well as grain quality traits will be assayed in all lines in all countri es. 
Moreover, nutritional traits such of storage of microelements and exclusion of toxic heavy metal will be measured in order 
to provide more robust seed characterization of the selected rice lines grown either in high salinity and no salinity 
conditions by UMIL. After large-scale trials, year 2019, at least 2 lines of each country (one from each variety)  will be 
sent to registry by the end-users of each Country so that they’ll be available to the rice-industry sector and rice-farming 
sector. 
 
WP5: Development of a wireless sensor network for remote salinity impact monitoring. 
  In order to monitor the salinity during the salt -stress field trials, a salinity remote detection system will be 
developed and implemented in selected pilot areas. The development of this sensor will be done in conjunction with the 
project end -users and rice farmers of the different rice producing European regions involved in this project.  The 
development of this  novel Wireless Sensor Network based on low cost electrical conductivity  sensors and an 
autonomous power supply based on energy harvesting will provide real time data of the salinity conditions of the rice 
paddies. This system will include a software package including a data-mining layer in which all the data collected in the 
fields will be used for improving the management of irrigation through a decision support system. It will serve to evaluate 
in real time the impact of the proposed adaptability interventions in response to salinity levels while ensuring the 
productivity and stability of the agricultural sector. This system will comprise a mesh of interconnected nodes acquiring 
salinity data, which will be remotely sent to a central server for data mining and the final output will be displayed through 
a user -friendly interfa ce for supporting irrigation decision making. The system will comprise energy harvesting 
technologies for being completely autonomous during the rice growing season and will allow the correct management 
and evaluation of the impacts on the proposed genetic and environmental interventions.

NEURICE  29 
 
WP6: Communication, d issemination, knowledge transfer and exploitation of results to the society, research 
centres and universities and the rice-farming sector.  
  With the aim of guaranteeing the proper transfer of the results obtained in this project, first of all a website will 
be put in motion for updating the progress of the different WPs as well as publications, posters and journal articles. It is 
expected for all research centres and universities to publish break through results as open-access papers as well as 
attend congresses and seminars to show the work generated by NEURICE project. Moreover, CRA, IRTA and CFR  will 
perform seminars and open field days in the years 2018 and 2019 to explain rice farmers how the new varieties should 
be used, how the monitoring systems created by IRIS work, and how to deal with salinity in rice paddies whether it is 
due to the climate change effects or to the saltwater treatments to stop the apple snail pest.  
 
WP7: Project management.  
In order to ensure a proper management of the project so that every partner do es their different tasks in all the 7 WPs 
as well as ensuring that funds are properly allocated UB will be the leader of this work package. Moreo ver, for 
coordinating all the 13 partners UB, UMIL and CIRAD will function as geographic nodes (one of each rice -producing 
region) establish a communication network to ensure that every partner receives the information needed to continue 
performing their corresponding WPs (Fig. 4). Finally, this WP will be in charge of carrying out and hosting the different 
meetings of the NEURICE project: kick-off meeting in 2016, annual meetings in 2017, 2018 and 2019 and last the project 
final meeting at beginning of 2020. Thus, this WP will expedite the functioning of the NEURICE project objectives.

Table 3.1a: Work package description 
 
Work package number  1 Start Date or Starting Event 2016-03-01 
Work package title Germplasm evaluation and genetic mapping for salt tolerance 
Participant number 1 4 5 6 8 9 
Short name of participant UB CRA UMIL UGLA INDEAR CAAS 
Person/months per participant: 15 28 30  12 34 20 
 
Objectives 
 
- Identification of new salt tolerant accessions within a worldwide japonica rice germplasm through biometric and 
physiological measurements. 
- Identification of loci involved in salt tolerance through GWAS and linkage mapping approaches. 
- Evaluation of allelic diversity in candidate salt tolerance genes through allele mining. 
- Detailed physiological characterization of the salt tolerant line FL478. 
 
Description of work  
 
This WP consists on the evaluation of rice germplasm in order to identify new salt tolerant accessions among worldwide 
japonica rice cultivars. It will be achieved through i) identification of new salt tolerant accessions in worldwide japonica rice 
cultivars, ii) identification of loci in the rice genome involved in conferring salt tolerance and iii) identification of the allelic 
diversity in candidate genes through bioinformatic analyses and allele mining. The information obtained in this WP will be used 
for the development of WP3 and WP4. Furthermore, this information provide new opportunities for the future of salt tolerance 
improvement in rice breeding programs. 
The lead partner of this WP is UMIL, which is working since many years on plant physiology and biochemistry of plant mineral 
nutrition and responses to abiotic stress. In particular, UMIL is an expert of phenotyping of abiotic stress response in rice and 
disposes the expertise, equipment and space for performing high quality phenotyping requested by this WP. Moreover, the 
activity of this WP will be completed by the high expertise of CRA, INDEAR and CAAS  in genotyping and bioinformatic 
analyses. 
 
Task 1.1. Phenotyping of germplasm collection and RILs for genome-wide association (GWAS) and linkage mapping 
studies. Contributors: UMIL and CRA. Months 1-24. 
A phenotyping activity will be conducted by UMIL on a germplasm collection of 300 japonica rice accessions and a biparental 
population of 200 F6 RILs obtained from a cross between a mild salt stress tolerant and salt susceptible rice genotypes. These 
accessions, supplied by CRA, will be screened for salt tolerance, in order to produce data for the GWAS and linkage mapping 
to be performed in Task 1.3 for the identification of loci involved in salt tolerance. For comparison, also FL478 and IR64-Saltol, 
the salt tolerance donors that will be used in WP2, will be phenotyped. Phenotyping will be  conducted on plants grown in pot 
filled with submerged soil in controlled greenhouse environment, both under control (i.e. no salinity) and salinity conditions.  
Each rice accession/line will be analyzed in triplicate (three different pots, each pot conta ining 12 -15 plants) from seed 
germination to flowering. For salt treatment, the electrical conductivity of the submerged soil will be weekly monitored and 
maintained around 5 dS/m adding, if necessary, adequate amounts of NaCl solution. The phenotyping activity, conducted for 
two years, will consist in: i) comparison of seed germination rate in saline and non-saline soil; ii) plants growth curve and leaf 
damages evaluation monitored at different phenological stages (4 -6 leaf, tillering and panicle initiatio n) by semi -automated 
photo cameras and dedicated software system; iii) leaf thermal imaging at different phenological stages (4-6 leaf, tillering and 
panicle initiation) using a semi-automated long-wave infrared cameras system; it represents a non-destructive protocol for the 
study of stomatal responses and the presence of stress-related symptoms iv) spikelet sterility  
Furthermore, a one-year phenotyping of a stronger salt treatment using a submerged soil with an electrical conductivity around 
10 dS/m will be conducted to identify possible highly tolerant accession, using a core collection expressly generated. To this 
purpose, after the first year of phenotyping, the germplasm will be divided in clusters, depending on the tolerance level to salt 
treatment. The tolerance data will be compared with genotypic data (molecular markers) to extract a core collection of a few 
genotypes, representative of the entire variability for salt tolerance in the whole germplasm collection. 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  33 
The most tolerant accessions, among the japonica accessions and the RILs, will be selected from the two -year phenotyping 
(salt treatment using the submerged soil with an electrical conductivity around 5 dS/m) and from the one -year phenotyping 
(salt treatment using the submerged soil with an electrical conductivity around 10 dS/m). These accessions will be 
characterized through physiological, biochemical and molecular analyses in WP3. 
 
Task 1.2. Detailed physiological characterization of the salt tolerant line FL478. Contributors: UB, UGLA. Mo nths 4-
25. 
An in-depth physiological study using 4 conditions of salinity on hydroponic culture (0, 50, 100 and 150 mM) will be carried out 
on the salt tolerant line FL478. Thus, mechanisms and processes that are known to operate in salt stress adaptation in plants 
will be examined in this line. In this respect, key mechanisms of salinity tolerance are the ability of a plant to control Na+ uptake 
and transport at both cellular and tissue levels and the exclusion and/or compartmentalization of Na+ (vacuoles). Accordingly, 
the following analyses will be carried out by UGLA on FL478: Na+ concentration measurements, shoot Na +/K+ ratio, Na + 
compartmentalization analysis by fluorescent laser scanning confocal microscopy of root tissue vacuoles (CoroNa+ staining), 
and direct electrophysiological methods to furthermore quantify Na + and K+ transport- and redistribution-related traits. UGLA 
will also perform a leaf chlorophyll content assay and membrane analysis consisting in assessment of membrane integrity 
through evaluation of electrolyte leakage and determination of major membrane sterols by GC/MS ICPOES. Moreover,  salt 
stress increases the production of reactive oxygen species (ROS) which, in excess, might cause oxidative damage to 
biomolecules (e.g. membrane lipids, thus, resulting in perturbation of cell membrane functioning). Reduced glutathione (GSH) 
protects the plant cell from the oxidative damage based on its redox buffering action by reducing ROS levels. Oxidative stress 
states produces peroxidation of lipid  membranes at the cellular level, to evaluate this, the levels of a well -known oxidative 
stress marker, malondialdehyde (MDA), will be measured. Biochemical markers of oxidative stress (ROS production and GSH 
and MDA levels) will be evaluated by UB to characterize salt-induced oxidative stress responses of the highly salt-tolerant line 
FL478. 
 
Task 1.3. GWAS and linkage analyses for the identification of loci involved in salt tolerance. Contributors: CRA, 
INDEAR, CAAS. Months 1-34. 
Loci involved in salt tol erance in the germplasm collection, already genotyped using  GBS with a coverage of about 55 .000 
SNPs, will be identified through a GWAS approach for salt stress treatment indicated in Task 1.1. For GWAS analysis, only 
SNPs with call-rate > 90% and MAF > 5%  will be used. The association between SNP genotypes and salt tolerance -related 
traits will be tested fitting one SNP at a time in a mixed linear model in which correction for population structure and kins hip 
matrix will be evaluated (CRA). RILs will be subjected to GBS for the construction of a SNPs-based genetic map and a linkage 
mapping procedure will be applied for the identification of genes/QTLs for salt stress tolerance using the phenotypic data 
produced under salt stress conditions (INDEAR). Linkage  analysis will be performed using CarthaGene or other suitable 
software. QTL mapping will be conducted with the R/qtl module of the R statistical computing pack age (or other suitable 
software) and threshold of significance for declaring presence of QTLs wi ll be identified through permutation analysis (CRA, 
INDEAR). Redundant markers in the two populations described in Task 1.1 will be removed before genetic studies. Linkage 
maps and QTL mapping results will be independently validated by the integrated software QTL IciMapping Version 4.0 (CAAS). 
 
Task 1.4. Bioinformatic analyses and allele mining. Contributors: CRA, INDEAR, CAAS, UMIL Months 24-36. 
An allele mining approach will be carried out for genes identified as candidates for the salt tolerant loci. For this purpose, the 
latest release of the Nipponbare genome sequence will be scanned for the identification of genes with functions compatible in 
conferring salt tolerance located in the genomic regions identified through GWAS and linkage mapping and theref ore 
representing candidate genes for the phenotypic effect of mild salt tolerance. UMIL will support the decision about candidate  
genes for salt tolerance on the basis of their putative functions. Candidate genes will be subsequently sequenced in a discrete 
number of tolerant and susceptible accessions through Illumina-based sequencing of PCR amplified fragments or targeted re-
sequencing-based procedures, depending from the number of candidates identified (CAAS, INDEAR, CRA, UMIL). Optimum 
breeding strategies to efficiently introduce favourable alleles to other elite parents will be investigated by computer simulation 
(CAAS). 
 
  
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.

Work package number  2 Start Date or Starting Event 2016-01-01 
Work package title Salt tolerance introgression 
Participant number 1 2 3 4 10 12 
Short name of participant UB CRAG CIRAD CRA CAMARA CFR 
Person/months per participant: 30 10 34.5 34 8 2 
 
Objectives 
 
- Obtain advanced lines with improved salt tolerance by introgressing salt tolerance alleles using marker assisted back-
crossing selection (MABCS). 
- Couple an embryo rescue technique adaptation with MABCS to fasten the introgression breeding process for obtaining 
the advanced salt tolerant lines. 
 
Description of work 
 
This WP consists in introgressing the salt tolerance alleles of FL476 indica rice into the selected elite European rice accessions. 
It will be ac hieved through a molecular marker assisted back -crossing selection (MABCS) breeding approach coupled to an 
embryo rescue (ER) technique adaptation that will be developed to fasten the back -crosses (BCs) introgression process to 
finally speed up the obtainm ent of advanced salt tolerant lines of the elite European rice lines. The MABCS program will be 
conducted to transfer the salt tolerance QTL region into 2 Spanish elite lines, (UB, CRAG and CAMARA), 2 Italian elite lines 
(CRA) and 2 French elite lines (CIRAD and CFR), in their respective greenhouses, paddy rice fields and laboratories. In order 
to avoid starting from donors with too low yield potential or photoperiod sensitivity, an advanced salt tolerant high -yielding 
indica line from the International Rice Research Institute (IRRI) called FL478, has been selected. This high productive and salt 
tolerant (recently introgressed with Saltol region from Pokkali) will be used as donor rather than the well -known tolerant 
landraces (Pokkali, Nona Bokra) to obtain productive European varieties in a shorter time than it would normally take. 
The leader partner of this WP is CIRAD, which has already practical experience in undertaking MABCS for different traits in 
rice. For the French elite lines, CIRAD will be in charge of the MABCS, whereas CFR will be in charge of the breeding process. 
For the Spanish lines, UB and CAMARA will perform the breeding process and embryo rescue, whereas the MABCS part of 
the process will be undertaken by CRAG. In Italy, the whole process (breeding, MABCS and embryo rescue) will be undertaken 
by CRA. 
 
Task 2.1, 2.2 and 2.3. BC1F1, BC2F1 and BC3F1 breeding . Contributors: UB, CRAG, CIRAD, CRA, CAMARA, CFR. 
Months (-1)-13. 
In all the backcrosses tasks, KASPar markers associated with the Saltol region on chromosome 1 will be used to select 
heterozygous plants for the introgressed segment on the carrier chromosome, and will be done by CRAG, CIRAD and CRA. 
In addition, a set of 60 -70 KASPar markers (available from the IBD platform; https://www.int egratedbreeding.net/) will be 
genotyped on the 11 non-carrier chromosomes to accelerate the return towards the recipient type, which will be also carried 
out by CRAG, CIRAD and CRA. To enable selecting the best beachhead plants as starting points for the program, the number 
of BC1F1 plants genotyped will be very large but the number of genotyped plants will decrease in the following BC generations 
 
Task 2.4. BC3F1 and BC3F2 selfing. Contributors: UB, CRAG, CIRAD, CRA. Months 11-22. 
From the BC3 generation, part of its F1 plants will be self -pollinated and in addition the KASPar markers set (available from 
the IBD platform; https://www.integratedbreeding.net/) will be genotyped on the 11 non-carrier chromosomes to accelerate the 
return towards the recipient t ype, which will be carried out by CRAG, CIRAD and CRA (Task 4). The resulting BC3F2 lines, 
with the smallest introgressed segment at the homozygous state and good return toward the recipient parent, will be selected 
and self-pollinated to obtain sufficient BC3F3 seeds for further phenotypical, physiological and genomical evaluation in WP3.

NEURICE  37 
 
Work package number  3 Start Date or Starting Event 2017-10-01 
Work package title Salt tolerance validation and mechanisms study 
Participant number 1 2 3 5 6 
Short name of participant UB CRAG CIRAD UMIL UGLA 
Person/months per participant: 12 47 10 22 40 
 
Objectives 
 
- Validation of BC3F3 salt tolerant lines and salt tolerant japonica rice cultivars/RILs accessions under none- and high-
controlled salinity conditions (hydroponic systems). 
- Physiological, biochemical and molecular characterization of the most promising salt tolerant introgressed rice lines and 
japonica rice cultivars/RILs accessions. 
- Identification of salt tolerance biomarkers in salt tolerant introgressed rice lines and japonica rice cultivars/RILs 
accessions. 
 
Description of work 
 
In this WP, we intend to establish a comprehensive view of determinants contributing to salt tolerance in BC3F3 introgressed 
rice lines produced in WP2, as well as in the japonica rice cultivars/RILs accessions selected in WP1. Salt tolerance will be 
evaluated in hydroponic systems under controlled greenhouse conditions (Task 3.1). Complementary approaches will be then 
used to investigate key mechanisms that control salinity tolerance in selected rice lines at the molecular, cellular and whol e 
plant levels (Tasks 3.2 to 3.4). To discover potential new salt tolerance determinants, expression profiling of the most promising 
introgressed lines will be used (Task 3.4). Finally, the information gained in these studies will be the basis for the identification 
of biomarkers for salt tolerance in rice (Task 3.5). 
The leader of this WP is CRAG, which is an expert in the study o f molecular and genetic characters of interest in plants, 
especially in plant response to environmental stress. CRAG disposes the expertise, equipment and space for performing high 
quality hydroponic systems to assay varieties, as well as the necessary exp ertise on transcript profiling and molecular 
mechanisms involved in salt stress tolerance in rice. UB, CIRAD, UMIL and UGLA will contribute to this WP. 
 
Task 3.1. Phenotypic selection for salt tolerance of selected introgressed rice lines. Contributors: CRAG, CIRAD, UMIL, 
UGLA. Month 21-26 
A forward screening of the BC3F3 lines generated in WP2 will be performed on hydroponically -grown plants at the seedling 
stage (15 day -old, no salinity and 100mM NaCl) under greenhouse conditions (CRAG, CIRAD, UMIL). For a comparison, 
FL478 and European parental lines will be included. Salt tolerance will be evaluated using the Standard Evaluation System 
(SES) established for rice by the International Rice Research Institute (IRRI).  
Then, the most promising salt tolerant lines, one from each variety and each country, will be analysed in detail in task 3.2, 3.3 
and 3.4 using 4 conditions of salinity on hydroponic culture (0, 50, 100 and 150 mM), through the evaluation of biochemical 
marker of oxidative stress, ion translocation, membrane integrity and transcript profiling. In addition, the six most salt-tolerant 
introgressed lines of each country, 3 lines from each variety, and the two most tolerant japonica rice cultivars/RILs accessions 
will be selected to be included in the Po delta field trials of 2018 (mid-scale) in WP4.  
 
Task 3.2. Physiological and biochemical characterization of salt-tolerant lines. Contributors: UB, CRAG, UMIL, UGLA. 
Month 27-36 
Selected introgressed lines identified in Task 3.1 will be examined to i dentify the physiological, biochemical and molecular 
mechanisms contributing to salt tolerance in these lines.  For this, the non-destructive phenotyping protocols (thermal imaging 
used for the phenotyping and chlorophyll fluorescence) will be used for the validation of salt tolerant lines (UMIL). Additionally, 
mechanisms and processes that are known to operate in salt stress adaptation in plants will be examined (UB, CRAG, UMIL, 
UGLA).  In this respect, a key mechanism of salinity tolerance is the ability of a plant to control Na + uptake and transport at 
both the cellular and tissue levels. The homeostasis of Na + and K +, and the exclusion and/or compartmentalization of Na + 
(vacuoles) are particularly important for salt tolerance. Salt stress also induces pr oduction of reactive oxygen species (ROS) 
which, in excess, might cause oxidative damage to biomolecules (e.g. membrane lipids), thus, resulting in perturbation of cell 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  38 
membrane functioning. Accumulation of malondialdehyde (MDA) is a well-known marker of membrane lipid peroxidation widely 
used as an indicator of salt-stress induced membrane damage . Reduced glutathione (GSH) protects the plant cell from the 
oxidative damage based on its redox buffering action by reducing ROS levels. Finally, a diverse set of  genes and signalling 
pathways are known to be regulated by salt stress that can be categorized according to their function (i.e. genes involved in  
protection against oxidative stress, synthesis of osmolites or ion transport, regulatory genes, among others).  
Accordingly, in this Task the following analyses will be carried out on selected salt -tolerant rice lines:  i) Na+ and K+ 
measurements on root, shoot  and xylem sap of Na+ and K+ will be performed by UMIL through ICP-MS to evaluate differences 
in Na+ and K+ systemic allocation in the whole plants for the considered BC3F2 and BC4F2 advanced rice lines. UGLA will 
also perform a leaf chlorophyll content assay. Na+ compartmentalization in rice roots will be examined at CRAG by fluorescent 
laser scanning confocal microscopy of root tissues (CoroNa+ staining). Biochemical markers of oxidative stress (GSH/GSSG 
ratio) (UMIL) and membrane lipid peroxidation (UB, UMIL, CRAG) will be evaluated to characterize salt -induced oxidative 
stress responses of the selected advanced rice lines. 
All these analyses will be performed also on six selected japonica rice cultivars/RILs accessions (two sensitive, two tolerant 
and two with an intermediate tolerant phenotype), derived from WP1 activities.   
 
Task 3.3. Membrane integrity, composition and function. Contributors: CRAG, UGLA, Month 27-33 
The assessment of membrane integrity will be carried out on salt-treated and non-treated selected rice lines by CRAG through 
evaluation of the relative electrolyte leakage, and voltage cla mp. The same plant material as in Task 3.2 will be used. The 
analysis of major membrane sterols (campesterol, β-sitosterol and stigmasterol will be approached by GC/MS (CRAG). Results 
obtained in these studies, together with those obtained in Task3.2 on membra ne lipid peroxidation, will allow us to establish 
whether there is a correlation between salt-induced membrane damage and tolerance to salt stress for the different rice lines 
here evaluated. 
 
Task 3.4. Transcript profiling of salt tolerant rice lines. Contributors: CRAG, UMIL. Month 27- 43 
Global gene expression analysis of the most promising introgressed rice lines (2 -4 lines) as demonstrated by their gain in 
tolerance to salinity will be carried out by CRAG (RNASeq, Illumina  HiSeq2000).  Leaves and roots of plants grown in control 
and salt conditions will be analysed. Prior to RNASeq analysis, the collected plant material will be validated by examining the 
expression of known salt -associated rice genes (RT -qPCR). Data arising from microarray experiments will be interpreted in 
the context of alterations in gene expression contributing to a phenotype of tolerance to salinity in introgressed rice lines. This 
analysis will also serve to identify salt-associated components and signalling pathways in rice, and confirm results obtained in 
regulation of Na+/K+ uptake/transport and protection against oxidative stress. Finally, salt tolerant candidate genes will be  
further evaluated by UMIL on the most promising introgressed rice lines and on the six selected japonica rice cultivars/RILs 
accessions (two sensitive, two tolerant and two with an intermediate tolerant phenotype). Since sulphur plays a pivotal role in 
the plant responses to abiotic stress, UMIL will further examine the expression pattern of key genes invo lved in sulphate 
assimilation. Among these key genes, the members of the adenosine -5'-phosphosulfate reductase (APS) family, as well as 
the members of the SULTR (sulphate transporter) family involved in controlling root-to-shoot sulphate translocation (Group 2) 
and sulphate concentration into the vacuole (Group 4)  will be evaluated. Other genes involved in the salt stress responses 
(e.g. the SOS pathway) will also be evaluated; other candidate genes will be specifically chosen in relation to the main 
characteristics observed during the activities in which the salt tolerant lines will be physiologically characterised.  
 
Task 3.5. Integration of data of physiological, biochemical and molecular markers of salinity tolerance of the 
introgressed rice lines. Contributors: CRAG, UMIL, UGLA. Month 44-46 
Data generated in WP3 together with those obtained in WP1 (electrophysiological studies) will be combined for systems 
analysis in order to identify determinants of salt tolerance in introgressed . This information will serve for the identification of 
biomarkers of salt tolerance in rice. Discovery of physiological, biochemical and molecular markers of salinity tolerance 
represents a potential value for rice breeding.

Work package number  4 Start Date or Starting Event 2018-03-01 
Work package title Field assays of the advanced breeding lines 
Participant number 1 4 5 7 10 11 12 13 
Short name of participant UB CRA UMIL IRTA CAMARA IRIS CFR SIS 
Person/months per participant: 11 16 17 39 40 9 25 20 
 
Objectives 
 
- Evaluation of WP3 selected rice lines in their respective fields of origin in mid-scale and large-assays scale in salinized 
and non-salinized fields (control). 
- Selection of the lines showing the best quality, best productivity and best commerciality to perform large scale field trials 
in WP5. 
 
Description of work  
 
Introgressed rice accessions validated in WP3 will be evaluated in the different European rice production regions in the summer 
of the years 2018 (mid-scale assay) and 2019 (large-scale assay) in salinized and non-salinized fields (control). Lines will be 
assayed in the rice producing regions of the partners involved including the end -users of the project to ensure a multi -actor 
approach that includes the research sector, the rice -industry sector and the rice -farming sector. At the end of the 2019 field 
trial, the NEURICE consortium will ensure that the end -users (CAMARA, CFR and SIS) will send to register at least 2 lines 
from each country (1 line from each variety used as parental line in the WP2).  Moreover, the most interesting japonica rice 
cultivars/RILs accessions identified in WP1 and WP3 will be analysed in the same way. 
The leader of this WP is CAMARA, which have large experience in rice breeding, new varieties development and certified rice 
seed production and commercialization. CRA and CFR will aid CAMARA to ensure that all the rice lines are evaluated in the 
rice paddy fields in which their parentals are normally sown. 
 
Task 4.1 and 4.2. 2018 and 2019 field trials. Contributors: UB, CRA, UMIL, IRTA, CAMARA, IRIS, CFR, SIS.  
The assays will be mid- and large-scale for years 2018 and 2019 respectively. Despite this, for both years, the procedure will 
be as following: 3 BC3F4 lines from each Spanish, Italian and French elite li nes (a total of 18 lines) coming from BC3F3 
selected accessions validated in the hydroponic assays of WP3 will be assayed in salinized and non-salinized fields. Lines will 
be tested in the natural growing area of their European parents, in this way, Italia n accessions will be tested in the Po river 
delta (SIS, CRA), Spanish lines in Ebro river delta (CAMARA, IRTA) and French accessions Rhône river delta (CFR). To be 
able to evaluate BC3F4 lines in terms of commercial potential (quality, productivity and cultivability) to ensure that the original 
recipient traits are maintained, the European elite parental lines will be included in both assays (salinized and non -salinized 
fields). Moreover, two salt tolerant japonica rice cultivars/RILs accessions, derived from WP1 will be assayed in salinized and 
non-salinized fields in all the locations. To ensure that the lines are salt tolerant, and at which extent, the FL478 salt tolerance 
donor will be also assayed in salinized field trials. Standard fertilization and field management principles of each growing area 
(country) will be applied. Parcels design will be the same in non -salinized and in fields destined to salinity tolerance assays, 
this will be done using a randomized design with 4 replications  in 4m 2 (2018 mid-scale trials) and 16 m 2 (2019 large-scale 
trials) plots/line distributed hazardously. Non-salinized field trials will be performed by CAMARA in Ebro delta (Amposta), CFR 
in Rhône delta (La Camargue North) and CRA in Po delta ( Vercelli) and SIS also in Po delta (Lagosanto-Ferrara), while 
salinized field trials will be conducted by IRTA in Ebro delta (Deltebre), CFR in Rhône delta (La Camargue South) and SIS in 
Po delta (Lagosanto FE). IRIS will monitor salinity using a Wireless Sensor Network for salinity in all salinized and non-salinized 
field trials in Ebro, Po and Rhône deltas. At least eight plants will be randomly selected from each line in order to record data 
measurements. General traits such as uniformity, plant shape and height, panicle number per plant, grain/panicle, phenological 
stage and pests/diseases appearances will be recorded weekly. More specific traits such as flag leaf width, length and angle, 
panicle position and exertion, days to heading, late flowering ratio and fun gal lesions on leav es and panicles  will be also 
recorded weekly. Plants will be harvested at  maturity to obtain proper yield results. Productivity, grain quality and industrial 
traits (head rice recovery, grain dimensions, amylose content, etc.) will be evaluated by CAMARA. Moreover, nutritional traits 
such of storage of microelements such as Fe and Zn, exclusion of toxic heavy metal such as Cd and As will be measured, in 
order to provide more robust seed characterization of the selected rice lines grown either in high salini ty and no salinity 
conditions by UMIL.

Work package number  5 Start Date or Starting Event 2016-02-11 
Work package title Development of a wireless sensor network 
Participant number 4 7 10 11 12 13 
Short name of participant CRA IRTA CAMARA IRIS CFR SIS 
Person/months per participant: 1 5 5 32 1 3 
 
Objectives  
 
- To gather specifications for establishing the requirements of the NEURICE Wireless Sensor Network (WSN). 
- To design and build a low cost WSN according to the NEURICE end-users design specifications. 
- To integrate all elements that make up the system into a functioning NEURICE unit. 
- To set up the system in a laboratory environment in order to carry out preliminary testing and fine-tuning 
- To perform field assays implementation tests and final installations in Spain, France and Italy 
 
Description of work 
 
Task 5.1. Review of technical requirements and end user design specifications. Contributors: CRA, IRTA, CAMARA, IRIS, 
CFR, SIS. Months 0-6. 
In this task the aim will be to gather qualitative input from a selected sample of European rice growers in order to formulate a 
collective up-to-date insight into their needs in terms of real time salinity monitoring and precision farming in order to define 
the specifications of the NEURICE system. In order to do this, a series of questionnaires and interviews will be performed 
following the Quality Function Deployment (QFD) methodology that aims at obtaining the most accurate vision from the end -
user needs. The results and conclusions arising from these consultations will be included in Deliverable 5.1 Technical 
requirements and end user specifications wh ich will include the system specifications (quantities to be measured and 
approximate range, accuracy and resolution) along with the key industry, market and regulatory requirements that influence 
on the development of the NEURICE system. These will form t he basis for detailed design specifications and performance 
characteristics of the NEURICE system concerning measurement range, accuracy, resolution, and operating conditions, as 
well as acquisition, maintenance and replacement costs for the sensor nodes. These user needs and requirements together 
with the technical specification of the overall NEURICE architecture will be used as a blueprint for guiding the technical wo rk 
to be carried out during Task 5.2, where the system will be designed, built and integrated, and Task 5.3 where the system will 
be preliminarily tested and fine-tuned. 
In parallel, during this task a thorough analysis of the market, regulatory and standardisation framework within which the 
proposed RICE-GUARD system will need to operate will be performed. To this end, during this task a review of all European 
and national regulatory related issues will be carried out in order to ensure that the system adheres to them, as well as to 
identify additional drivers for the technology. The results of this task will feed into Deliverable 5.1. IRIS will lead this task with 
the assistance of IRTA and CRA, as well as the agricultural SMEs of the project, CAMARA, CFR and SIS. 
 
Task 5.2. Design, manufacturing and integration of the NEURICE system. Contributor: IRIS. Months 7-15. 
Results from task 5.1 will be used to propose designs for the sensor nodes and the instrumentation electronics, the network, 
software and User Interface in order to fulfil the user requirements. The proposed NEURICE system will rely first and foremost 
on sensory data from its environment. This sensory data will come from multiple sensors in distributed locations. Information  
about nodes surroundings will need to be known as well as their internal workings. To this end the system wil l be designed 
and built to ensure that it is capable of detecting, monitoring and collecting the data, as well as assessing and evaluating the 
information before finally transmitting it. The design and building of the NEURICE system will be reported on Del iverable 5.2: 
Design and manufacturing of the NEURICE prototype. IRIS will lead this task. For accomplishing this task, the electronic 
components (PCB boards, power supply units) for the sensor, control and communication parts of the sensing nodes will be 
designed based on the user requirements and the environmental characteristics of the area to be monitored . Since the 
selection of components may affect the individual work in other tasks, the timing programme has been carefully planned to 
ensure that this task starts in the early stages of system design in order to ensure a smooth development that avoids the high 
costs associated with subsequent re-designing. 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  43 
The proposed RICE-GUARD system consists of a heterogeneous wireless sensor network with several basic nodes and a 
single master node  for a large area. In both cases, each node will conceptually comprise a sensor unit  (SU) and a 
communication unit (CCU), and a power supply system based on solar energy harvesting.  
The variety of available technologies ne cessitates a thorough review of potential components, to ensure that an optimal 
selection is made to ensure a consistent, reliable, robust overall system is designed. In addition, an evaluation of current sensor 
technologies will be carried out and suitable technology will be selected for further development and implementation. Then, a 
draft of the physical design of the prototype will be done and later improved as it incorporates the changes needed. The 
mechanical structure will comprehend the shape, size and materials used. 
The mechanical design of the prototypes must take into account not only material endurance to the harsh environment, 
corrosion by salty water and fauna, but also weight limitations and resistance to physical stress. In that sense, the casing will 
be selected or developed to comply with the appropriate Index Protection, which will be at least equal to IP 65. 
The battery system deserves special attention. Different batteries will be evaluated following the criteria of offered voltage, life-
time and rechargeable capacity by solar panels. The solar panels needed to recharge the batteries will also be selected. This 
task will address the placement of the battery, the solar panel and the regulator to interconnect them if needed. 
The information required by NEURICE will be provided by a Distributed Wireless Sensor Network, which will be responsible 
for sensing, as well as for first stages of the processing hierarchy. This purpose will be achieved optimizing the protocol to be 
used in NEURICE node s, focussing on low -power technologies to enhance the battery life of the system. A heterogeneous 
WSN (with water electrical conductivity sensors) will be designed for monitoring the salinity in the study areas. The final number 
of nodes will be defined fo llowing the requirements defined within Task 5.1 in order to ensure the proper environmental 
monitoring of the pilot areas of the NEURICE project. Based on the results of Task 5.1 and on the analysis on the dimensions 
and communication distance capabilitie s of the WSN the final configuration and network topology will be established. The 
selection of the wireless technology will also have to take into account the frequency bands available for free use. ISM bands 
are unlicensed and therefore they have no cost  associated in their use. However, not all technologies are available in every 
band and the available equipment may be limited in some of them. The study of the most suitable band with special 
consideration about the attenuation of the signal will influence the selection of the wireless technology. 
Moreover, the different technologies in order to select the best and most suitable telecommunication technology for the 
transmission of the packets filled with the sensory data from the gateway to the central server will be evaluated. The gateway 
is the device that will be used as the central on -field point in the NEURICE network. It will act as the highest hierarchy node 
within the network, and will have bigger computational capabilities than the rest of the nodes. A local database on the gateway 
will store the readings from the nodes, taking care of its identification and the timestamp from each of the measurements and 
safeguarding the sensor information in case of communication problems to the central server. The gateway will have different 
connection options to be able to transmit the information from inside the field to a remote central server database, so that the 
system will be able to adapt to the facility’s needs. The information will be sent to a central d atabase that will serve a dual 
purpose: (a) to control the NEURICE system and, (b) to act as a user interface with the system. The database software will act 
as the back-end of the system. This back-end system will be responsible for network control; it will receive the data sent form 
the NEURICE sensors over the WSN and this data will be processed by the database software. This task will design both 
databases (local and central) to meet the requirements from the partners considering the data that the syste m will need to 
handle and store.  
The building of the system software and the web-based user interface represents an important component of the NEURICE 
architecture and the central point to the innovation of the system. In order to process the data, along with the requests submitted 
via end users to the web portal, a specific web -based application that will build on existing “open -source” solutions will be 
developed. The User Interface will need to be designed and implemented to access the database and present the results from 
the data collection in an understandable and customisable form. The objective will be that the final user gets familiarised quickly 
with the interface and can adapt the presentation of the data in the most appropriate way for his or he r needs in order to 
improve their management practises and resources . The aim is to develop this easy to use, readily accessible user 
interface that also allows different kinds of representations of the data and improves the management practises in terms of 
apple snail eradication and validation of new salt resistant rice varieties. During this task, extensive user tests will be performed 
to ensure that the design meets the needs and expectations of the end-users of the NEURICE system.  
All the different co mponents that make up the NEURICE system will be integrated together to physically build the complete 
NEURICE prototype. Specific models of mechanical (material, holders, screws...) and electronic (PCB and processors 
involved) parts will be evaluated and selected. The overall objective will always be obtaining the most competitive cost for the 
system while retaining the required quality of functionality in line with the system specifications defined in Task 5.1. Off -the-
shelf materials and tools will be preferred over tailor-made ones whenever available. In addition, not only the costs for a small 
number of prototypes but also the costs of a later large-scale production will be evaluated.  
 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.

Task 5.3. Preliminary prototype testing and fine-tuning. Contributors: CRA, IRTA, CAMARA, IRIS, CFR, SIS. Months 
16-23. 
Once all the elements have been fully integrated into the NEURICE unit, it is vital that preliminary laboratory and field tes ting 
is carried out in order to ensure that the integrated components work at peak performance and smoothly together. During these 
laboratory trials the NEURICE system will be fine-tuned and adjusted as necessary, before the NEURICE prototype system is 
deemed ready for field-testing. Then, the system will be tested under field conditions with the supervision and collaboration of 
partners of the NEURICE project: CRA, IRTA, CAMARA, CFR and SIS . This task will be led by IRIS and will involve the 
planning of the functional tests and their execution. The results will be analysed and a repo rt will be drawn up documenting 
the results (Deliverable 5.3). 
 
Task 5.4. Field assays implementation tests. Contributors: CRA, IRTA, CAMARA, IRIS, CFR, SIS. Months 26-45. 
Following the integration of the definite NEURICE prototype and its preliminary validation at laboratory and field level it will be 
necessary to plan field tests in different paddy field sites. To this end, the NEURICE system will be installed by IRIS, test ed 
and validated at the sites of the participating agricultural SMEs - CFR in France, CAMARA in Spain and SIS in Italy. The editing 
of a comprehensive installation and user manual will be required and annexed to D5.4. An analysis of the results of these tests 
will allow the specifications of accuracy and resolution of the salinity measur ements to be validated, along with the sampling 
frequency and the minimum duration of the batteries. They will also ensure that the system is robust enough to withstand the 
harsh environment. The obtained results will be documented in Deliverables 5.4 “2018 Field assays implementation tests” and 
5.5 “2019 Field assays implementation tests”. 
A careful plan for the in -field testing will be drawn in close collaboration with the rice growers in the consortium who will be 
testing the system in their rice paddies with the help of CRA, CFR, CAMARA, IRTA and SIS  who will perform a comparative 
analysis of the salinity measured in-field and the salinity tests performed with the newly developed rice varieties. 
 
Deliverables 
 
D5.1: Technical requirements and end user specifications [By: IRIS; Type: R; Delivery date: M11]. Report on the technical 
requirements and end user needs to generate a detailed specifications document to be used as an input for the design.  
D5.2: Design and manufacturing of the NEURICE prototype [By: IRIS; Type: R; Delivery date: M23]. Report describing the 
detailed designs of the system and manufacturing characteristics such as materials, procedure and user manual. 
D5.3: Preliminary testing and fine-tuning report [By: IRIS; Type: R; Delivery date: M24]. Report describing the outcomes of 
the first tests performed for validating the system and fine-tuning the overall functionality.   
D5.4: Field assays implementation tests [By: IRIS; Type: R; Delivery date: M32 and M44]. 2018 and 2019 assays. Report 
describing detailed results from the tests in the field to monitor salinity in different European areas. 
 
Milestones

Work Package Title Communication, dissemination, knowledge transfer and exploitation of results

Objectives  
The aim of WP 6 is to ensure a wide dissemination of the new rice salt tolerant varieties and the salinity sensor developed in 
this project in order to facilitate their adoption amongst stakeholders.  
The main objectives of this WP are: 
- To widely disseminate and transfer to stakeholders the new technologies developed (salt-tolerant varieties and the 
wireless sensor networks works) and instruct them about their management and how to deal with salinity in rice 
paddies in order to mitigate the imminent effects of salinization and deterioration of water quality in the 
Mediterranean basin due to climate change and to avoid the decline in production observed when seawater 
treatments are applied to control the apple snail 
- To exchange with the scientific community the results of this project in an accessible and open manner 
- To communicate and disseminate the goals, progresses and all the information related to the project to the society 
and administrations so increase their awareness into the consequences of climate change in food production. 
The specific objectives are: 
- To identify the major stakeholders. 
- To disseminate the new rice salt tolerant varieties to rice farmers, rice millers and consumers. 
- To introduce the salinity wireless sensor as a tool to manage salinized rice field. 
- To disseminate the technology for apple snail control developed in the project. 
- To exchange with the scientific community the most relevant achievements of the project.  
 
 
Description of work 
This WP will focus on ensuring proper and adequate ways to disseminate and transfer the results and information generated 
by NEURICE project to the rice farming sector, technicians and rice seed industries which will benefit from the new varieties 
obtained and wireless sensor network developed in this project, as well as to the society, administrations, research centres 
and universities to raise public awareness of the issue on climate change and its effects on food production. 
The leader of this WP is IRTA, which has been designated as expert of the Spanish national committee for the evaluation of 
new rice varieties while also has a wide experience in rice experimentation. IRTA rice activities give prominence to technology 
transfer, being permanently in contact with stakeholders: farmers rice industry, technic ians and government officers. IRTA 
organizes twice a year crop events, open field days and technical conferences, which have been consolidated not only locally 
but also at national scale since it counts with the attendance of national stakeholders. Therefore, they are an excellent platform 
to disseminate results from the  NEURICE project to the rice farming sector and rice producing industries  IRTA has also a 
Communication Department with experience in agrifood European active projects ( www.itaca-project.com, 
www.cleanleach.eu) or recently initiated (i3Food, GreenRice) capable to produce all kind of materials and formats for the 
dissemination and communication of the NEURICE project.

Once the project is finished, a detailed report is prepared that will include all it has been done for communicating and spreading 
the project, as well as the impacts, the materials and/or actions generated. 
Task 6.1. Communication of results. Contributors: UB, CRAG, CIRAD, CRA, UMIL, UGLA, IRTA, INDEAR, CAAS, 
CAMARA, IRIS, CFR, SIS. Months 1-48 
In this task, first, we will design a NEURICE logo and image as well as a NEURICE website. Then, the NEURICE consortium 
will establish the periodic sending of a newsletter. Information about the progress of the project will be also updated on social 
networks and by generating press notes and videos.  
The NEURICE logo and image will ensure that the project will be visible to everybody and will be shown along with the 
WEBSITE launch. This website will be the centre of the d issemination in the NEURICE project and will contain different web 
sections for professionals as well as general visitors and medias  to describe the objectives, general information and other 
contents (press notes, videos, photos of the project, etc.) of the NEURICE project. Moreover, it will also serve as a platform for 
researchers and rice seed industries interested in the project to contact any of the partners involved. Finally, the website will 
be linked not only with other websites but also with NEURICE  newsletter and NEURICE social networks. The newsletter will 
be sent periodically by the project partners to subscribers and social networks, and will include the latest news, activities , 
videos, etc. Several social networks related with the project (agric ultural, agrigenomics, genetics…) and more general ones 
such as: Linked-in, Twitter and Facebook will be used, which will be linked with the social networks of different partners. All of 
the activities, news, general information, inquiry results, workshops , etc., will be diffused by one or more dissemination 
channels of the project (web, newsletter, social networks…) along with videos about NEURICE projects such as general 
interviews, workshops, and webinars. In addition, a series of leaflets and brochures will explain the project, the concepts and 
the results. These materials will be located in the website, newsletters, social networks, sent to the media, etc. 
Task 6.2. Dissemination of results. Contributors: UB, CRAG, CIRAD, CRA, UMIL, UGLA, IRTA, INDEAR, CAAS, 
CAMARA, IRIS, CFR, SIS. Months 1-48. 
Activities oriented towards results dissemination will consist mainly in open -access papers as well as conference 
communications. The partners of the NEURICE consortium will compromise to publish breakthrough rese arch findings in: i) 
relevant international scientific journals with high impact factor, which can be measured according to the times that each article 
can be cited; ii) open-access papers to allow the information to be available to all interested research es in Europe as well as 
other rice producing regions all over the world. Moreover, the results of the project will be shown in conferences as oral 
communications as well as posters to ensure that results are shown in events aimed to specific sectors such a s plant 
physiology, plant genomics, rice production, etc. 
Task 6.3. Knowledge transfer and exploitation of results. Contributors: UB, CRA, IRTA, CAMARA, IRIS, CFR, SIS.  
Months 27-47. 
Activities oriented towards knowledge transfer and exploitation of result s to the seed industry and rice farmers will be mainly 
by open field days and cooperatives. IRTA, CFR and CRA will instruct the seed industry and rice cooperatives rice farmers 
how the new varieties should be used and how they will benefit of them. To do t his they will conduct seminars and open field 
days directed to rice farmers with the objective of guaranteeing the proper transfer of the results obtained in this project. These 
working sessions will ensure that explainations are given to the rice farming sector on how the new varieties should be used 
to deal with salinity in rice paddies whether it is due to the climate change effects or to the saltwater treatments to stop the 
apple snail pest. In addition, a plan for transmitting the information and innov ations obtained in this project to the rice seed 
producing industries will be implemented to show how the wireless sensor network developed by IRIS to monitorize salinity in 
real-time works along with the new varieties. 
The expected results from the project will be continually assessed in terms of novelty, patentability and protection in Sub-
task 6.3.1. Protection of the IPR  as part of an effective  knowledge management strategy. Results shall be owned by the 
participant generating them in accordance to a pr otocol of procedures that will be defined, which will be followed by each 
partner to clearly show the development of the generation of knowledge or results. In cases where the results are generated 
jointly (i.e. where the separate parts of some result cannot be attributed to different participants), it will be jointly owned. The 
allocation and the terms of exercising this joint ownership will be agreed in Joint Ownership Agreements that will be established 
during Sub-task 6.3.2. IPR Ownership and sharing. Access rights to results for implementing the project will be granted on 
a royalty-free basis. Access rights for use purposes will be granted either royalty-free, or on fair and reasonable conditions 
to be agreed in the NEURICE Exploitation Agreement.

Objectives  
 
- To coordinate the project between the partners and the European Commission To coordinate the steering 
committee as well as the group of the WP leaders in order to ensure that all NEURICE beneficiaries and in 
particular the WP leaders will carry out the work plan as it has been scheduled 
- To prepare protocols and to ensure that all the fields of the NEURICE will be carried out according to scheduled 
work plan  
- To consolidate the NEURICE results in to periodic reports  
- To deliver the financial periodic cost statements to EU 
- To create the Advisory Board that will consult the NEURICE project 
 
 
Description of work  
This WP will focus on the integration of data and results from all the others work packages in order to ensure proper information 
exchange between partners and to make NEURICE project visible. The leader of this WP is UB, since it is the coordinator of 
the NEURICE project, who has coordinated other agricultural projects such as OPTICHINA and TERPMED.  
UB manages an average of 150 European projects per year, for an average amount of about 8.6 million euro a year. 
 
Task 7.1. Project coordination and management. Contributors: UB. Months 0-47. 
The coordination of the project will be accomplished through the technical meetings held regularly, with respect to the project 
planning and timetable. Special attention will be given to the preparation of the kick -off, annual and final meetings. All WP 
leaders (in close collaboration with the Task leaders of their WPs) as appointed in the project outline, shall have protocols (or 
action plan) and updated time schedules, which will be though discussed, finalized and accepted by all partners during the 
kick-off meeting. They shall ensure that that the accepted protocol (or action plan) is realistic and will lead to the collection of 
high quality, up-to-date data. Possible adjustment to the predicted time schedule may be required, depending on the approved 
project starting date. This issue shall also be addressed and finalized in the kick-off meeting. 
At the kick -off meeting the WP leaders apart from the protocol (or the action plan) have to present in detail the resources 
(reports from completed projects, ongoing research actives and sites, international liter ature, etc.) that will use as a base in 
order to run their work packages. In order to achieve an efficient coordination and management of the project, a steering 
committee will be established soon after the beginning of the project, which will consist by the coordinator and the WP leaders. 
The steering committee will meet in every technical meeting of the project. 
 
Task 7.2. Steering Committee. Contributors: UB. Months 0-47. 
The Steering Committee is the decision-making body of the project. Chaired by the project Coordinator, it is composed of one 
representative per partner (including work package leaders), each having one vote for decision -making. The Steering 
Committee will be in charge of the operational management of all activities of the Project and re -orientation whenever 
necessary, budget revision, incorporation of new contractors, measures towards defaulting partners. It will integrate 
recommendations from the IPR strategy  and Dissemination Committee and survey ethical and gender issues. 
The Steering  Committee will also be in charge of financial management of work packages. The Steering Committee will 
supervise the work of the European Project Manager including quality control and preparing meetings with the EC, including 
preparation and transmission of deliverables. 
 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  50 
Task 7.3. Advisory Board. Contributors: UB. Months 0-47. 
External international leading scientific experts, representatives of industry, breeders, agronomists, physiologists, etc. wi ll be 
integrated in an Advisory Board (AB). The AB will provide guidance to the Steering Committee on project orientations. It will 
be consulted by the Steering Committee on all relevant important scientific issues and can make any proposal or transmit any 
information it seems useful to the Steering Committee. The external expert panel will provide an opportunity for getting on 
board additional industrial partners, together with others stakeholders. 
The AB will share information with the steering committee through newsletters, e -mails, videoconference and forum on 
NEURICE website. With the aim of sharing knowledge during the project activities, a selected number of specialists in the field 
of plant and crop physiology, agronomy, biotechnology, environmental researchers, and from industries, belonging to the AB, 
will be invited at the annual NEURICE meetings in order to investigate specific issues based on the activity needing. Prior to  
the beginning of its activity, each AB members will enter into a non-disclosure agreement. 
 
Task 7.4. Consortium agreement. Contributors: UB. Month 0. 
The Consortium Agreement will be a single formal legal document, agreed and signed by all the parties which defines a set of 
standard conditions under which the project will be managed and IP will be shared.  
The Consortium Agreement will:  
 be coherently documented;  
 provide an appropriate project management framework;  
 clearly allocate responsibility for resource allocation and risk management;  
 reflect the understandings of the parties as to their role, rights and responsibilities; en sure that the work for which 
funding is allocated is completed in a timely fashion. 
The Consortium Agreement will be drawn and signed in the first three months of the project. 
 
Task 7.5. Mid-term evaluation. Contributors: UB. Month 24. 
After two years project a mid-term evaluation will be asked to the Commission in order to assess the on-going activities of the 
project for each of the planned WPs. 
 
Task 7.6. NEURICE projects meetings. Contributors: UB, CRAG, CIRAD, CRA, UMIL, UGLA, IRTA, INDEAR, CAAS, 
CAMARA, IRIS, CFR, SIS. Months 1-47. 
The following meetings are planned during the duration of the NEURICE project:  
Kick-off meeting: this meeting will be held in Barcelona at the beginning o f the NEURICE project (02/2016)  in order to: 
organize all the initial  work, make a fresh start of the different work packages, coordinate partners activities, as well as to 
implement and execute the work packages. It will also be established that all partners involved in each Work Package should 
communicate periodically.  
Project development discussion meeting year 1 and 2: At the beginning of the years 2017 and 2018, a project development 
discussion and coordination meeting is proposed, which will take place in the different rice regions at January of each year.  
These meetings will serve to monitor if any of the proposed risks is present and to monitor the work packages development: 
Have deliverables be met? Have milestones been achieved? Moreover, this are foreseen during January of each year to be 
able to report in time to the EC, which in term will allow to liaise between the project partners and the EC programme officers.  
Field monitoring and meeting year 2 and 3: This two meeting will be held during the summer of 2018 and 2019 so partners 
of the NEURICE project can discuss the develop pment of the project as well as monitor the field trials of 2018 and 2019. 
Final meeting: At the end of the project in January 2020 a results meeting to gather and discuss the results and achievements 
will be proposed at Brussels, Belgium.

3.2 Management structure and procedures  
 
3.2.1  Coordination and management 
The coordinator of the NEURICE project is the ‘Universitat de Barcelona’, represented by Dr. Salvador 
Nogués. His primary role is to represent the intermediary between the European Commission and the Consortium as 
well as to be the promoter and supervisor of the overall technical and scientific progress of NEURICE (Fig. 7). 
The Coordinator will be responsible, among other  tasks defined by the EC Contract and the Consortium Agreement 
for:  
 Chairing the Steering Committee and taking all actions to enable proper decision making by this decision 
body.  
 Ensuring smooth operation of the project: work plan maintenance, monitoring project progress, analysing 
result, identification of trouble and consequences for the future research.  
 Writing periodic reports on progress of the project, partner activity.  
 Submitting all required progress reports, deliverables and financial statement s to the European 
Commission.  
 Communicating all information in connection with the Project to the Commission.  
 Transferring the advanced payments and further payments to the participants as per the provisional 
budget and the actual expenses approved by the Steering Committee. 
 
The WP Leaders are in charge of monitoring all activities towards the objectives of their WP. They will take any operational 
decision regarding the WP day-to-day management. They will be in charge of preparing the decisions to be taken by the Steering 
Committee and ensuring that these decisions are properly implemented. They will be also in charge of addressing and 
documenting internal risks which may impair the progress towards the objectives of the WP and suggest strategies to anticipate 
and minimize such internal risks.  
In order to achieve an efficient coordination and management of the project, a steering committee will be established soon after 
the beginning of the project consisting from the coordinator and one representative per partner. 
The Consortium Agreement to be signed by all participants will include specific provisions covering the ownership, protection and 
dissemination of the project results as well as provisions explaining how access can be gained to them. Responsible  for the 
monitoring and correct functioning of such provisions will be the coordinator (UB, Spain) which will ensure that any future I PR 
provisions officially notified by the EC is included in the Description of Work and/or in the consortium Agreement. It will cover in 
more detail the aspects described below. 
Furthermore, the Consortium Agreement will also cover other issues such as : the time-limit for the prior notice to the rest of the 
partners, as well as the necessary information concerning the envisaged new owner of the foreground to assure the other partners 
can exercise their access rights. The time limit for objecting to any transfer of ownership, when a partner demonstrates that their 
access rights would be adversely affected.  The rules for the adeq uate and effective protection of the foreground capable of 
industrial or commercial application, having due regard to the legitimate and commercial interests of all partners. 
 
 
3.2.2.  Project manager 
Given the range of partners and work involved, the project will require dedicated and experienced project management 
to ensure that the objectives, time-scales and anticipated deliverables are met and that the overall budget and the specific sub -
project allocations are effectively monitored. This will be achie ved through the allocation of an experienced project manager, 
supporting the technical administration of the Project by the Coordinator (Partner 1, Universitat de Barcelona) with overall 
responsibility for the Project’s coordination and management. 
 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  57 
Project Manager (PM): PM is responsible for the overall technical objectives achievements and reports to Project Coordinator. 
In this function:  
 
 PM prepares and presents the consolidated technical reports needed by the Project Coordinator.  
 PM ensures the overall technical and scientific consistency of the project  
 Follow up work progress very closely by reviewing work progress reports;  
 Exchange information regularly with WP leaders (WPL);  
 Ensure that information is circulating between WP leaders (WPL);  
 Organize and chair scientific meetings at least each 6 months.  
 Organize and chair any additional technical meeting ensuring the technical consistency of the Project.  
 The Project Manager will be appointed by the Project coordinator with the agreement of the Steering Comitee. 
 
 
3.2.3.  Steering Committee 
The Steering Committee is the decision -making body of the project. Chaired by the project Coordinator, it is 
composed of one representative per partner (including work package leaders), each having one vote for decision-
making. The Steering Committee will be in charge of the operational management of all activities of the Project and re-
orientation whenever necessary, budget revision, incorporation of new contractors, measures towards defaulting 
partners. It will integrate recommendations from the Intellectual Property Use and Dissemination Committee and survey 
ethical and gender issues. The Steering Committee will also be in charge of financial management of work packages. 
The Steering Committee will supervise th e work of the European Project Manager  including quality control and 
preparing meetings with the EC, including preparation and transmission of deliverables. Chaired by the Coordinator, 
the Steering Committee is composed of the following persons, each of th em holding both scientific excellence and
