NEURICE  61
3.3 Consortium as a whole  
 
3.3.1 Consortium description 
 
The NEURICE consortium proposes an equilibrium between public research and technological development universities 
(UB, UMIL, UGLA, CAAS) and private technological and farmer companies (CAMARA, CFR, SIS, IRIS). Moreover, in NEURICE 
there are research centres (CRAG, IRTA, CRA, CIRAD, INDEAR) involved which have wide experience in public research and 
private development. Thus, the consortium is whole and is complemented between all partners, and will surely integrate the work 
between all of the parties involved. 
With the idea of develop ing European salt tolerance rice varieties, it is imperative that the consortium has both, the knowledge 
and research experience of the universities and research c entres and the competence of the private companies to validate, 
register and commercialize the accessions generated. Thus, the partners  have well defined roles in laboratory research or field 
trials and  complement one another, covering the possible weak points of the consortium. 
Additionally, a benefit is that the majority of the partners are familiar with one another and have participated in other projects  
together; some of them working with rice (see Fig. 8). For example CIRAD, CFR, CRAG, IRTA and CRA,  are currently 
collaborating within the GREENRICE project, a European project funded by the FACCE -ERA-NET+ call on Climate Smart 
Agriculture, to evaluate the efficiency of a n Alternate Wetting and Drying rice production system (AWDS). The implications of 
AWD system on the rice environment and productivity is assessed in the project through monitoring of water consumption, soil 
salinity, plant x soil x microbial community interactions, GHG emission, soil chemistry and through the identification of rice cultivars 
that maintain their productivity under AWDS as well as the traits that contribute to this adaptability.  
 
 
Figure 8. Scheme showing the partners relations in different projects . Partners are represented by white -filled blue 
rectangles, projects by colored rectangles and other collaborations by dotted rectangles. 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  62 
CRAG and CIRAD ha ve worked together before in other projects like EUROOT, and CRA has worked with UMIL in several 
projects like POLORISO or RISINNOVA (rice breeding and technology improvement) and have joint PhD programs. Furthermore, 
CRA has worked in the MARS project with SIS. Connecting with the other partners, IRTA has participated in some projects with 
CAMARA, IRIS and CFR together, like SMARTPADDY (a project to measure and manage salinity in rice fields) or RICEGUARD 
(a project to develop a wireless sensor network to predict rice blast). 
CRA, UMIL and CIRAD are collaborating in a project entitled “Genomic selection for resources use efficiency in rise- GS-RUSE” 
funded by Agroplis Foundation  (FR) and Cariplo Foundation (I) in the framework of the “French -Italian Rice Science and 
Technology Initiative”. The GS-Ruse project aims at contributing to tackle some of the conceptual issues of GS in plants and at 
providing rice breeders with tailored methods and tools for the integration of GS approach in their breeding strategies. 
 
UB has worked with other kind of projects and research activities with CRAG, CAMARA and IRTA. Actually is common the flow 
of knowledge and students between this partners because UB and IRTA are part of the CRAG consortium. Moreover, UB has an 
industrial PhD program based on rice with CAMARA and diverse PhD programs with UGLA. UB also has participated in European 
projects with the two international countries, in the OPTIMA project with INDEAR and in the OPTICHINA project with CAAS.  
 
3.3.2 Industrial/commercial involvement 
 
The NEURICE project will secure a full exploitation of the results generated. It will also generate findings that can be 
exploited commercially, like new salt tolerant rice varieties, salinity wireless sensor network prototype and decision support system 
software , see Table 2.2.c.). To achieve this goal, several SMEs (i.e. CAMARA, CFR, SIS and IRIS) are involved as farming 
partners. A description of these p artners can be found in Section 1.3.3. To maximize the commercial and industrial impact the 
consortium will be linked directly to the agricultural European Innovation Partnership (EIP -AGRI) featuring direct access to 
technological solution providers. In ad dition, an external advisory board formed by internationally recognized scientists and 
managers will participate in general coordination meetings and providing assessment of on the project development (see above). 
This will ensure cross -sector dissemination as well as promoting a direct dialogue between researchers and practitioners at a 
local, regional and international level.  
There is strong industry leadership and involvement in this consortium. Each industry participant has clear expectations and 
commitments towards commercially using the results of this project in their businesses, which is manifested through the initial 
exploitation and business plans presented in Section 2.2.  
While the involvement of industry in R&D consortia increases the success r ate of market -oriented exploitation, vertical 
integration (i.e. including the whole value chain) in R&D projects is a success factor for market-oriented exploitation. To this 
end, NEURICE includes technology SME companies (IRIS) and agricultural SMEs (CAMARA, CFR, SIS) with research performing 
capacity who can contribute to technology push, who are not only capacitated to contribute to the R&D effort, especially in the 
context of scale-up, integration and demonstration of the results during the project, but who can absorb the knowledge 
generated to protect it, in order to further develop and industrialise the outputs post-project towards commercialisation. The 
inclusion of SMEs will contribute end-user industry knowledge and experience to assist in mainstreaming the results of the project 
and in validating them in the field. Market actors (IRIS, SIS) will contribute to the exploitation pathways for the project results 
platform. They will also enable demand to be stimulated as a result of the market pull. Impo rtantly, the contacts with large 
enterprises can make a difference in successful market oriented exploitation as long as the research outcomes are in line wit h 
their ‘expectations’. NEURICE has secured the interest and involvement of this industry at the early stages of the preparation of 
this bid, and they all understand its scope and have been very committed in collaborating with the rest of the partners to contribute 
to the definition of the project. Their engagement during the proposal preparation stage  has helped to shape the scope and 
ambition of this bid. 
 
3.3.3 Other countries 
 
INDEAR: the participation of INDEAR is essential for the project because has the most advanced agro-biotech research platforms 
in Latin America, including a high performance D NA sequencing platform, essential for the NEURICE project. This Genomic 
capability is necessary for the project to accomplish the large genomic analyses to be done in WP1. Additionally, in the last  
decade Argentina has increased their rice production in a 121%, accompanied of an increase in the yield of 16%, and has 
increased their exportation in a 233%, principally to Brazil (Report “Informe de Coyuntura” of “Alimentos Argentinos” of the 
This proposal version was submitted by salvador NOGUES on 11/06/2015 15:44:52 CET. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
NEURICE  63 
Argentinian Minister of Agriculture, livestock and fisheries) . Thus , INDEAR offers a great opportunity to internationalize the 
European rice varieties produces in the NEURICE project to the South American rice market. 
 CAAS: China is the World leading rice producer , so its involvement in a rice project is mandatory. The wid e knowledge, 
technological advances and competence are advantageous values for the NEURICE project. As this project uses European rice 
varieties, the implication of CAAS in the laboratory and field trials is not so necessary, but it is in the bioinformatics of the genomic 
analysis. CAAS is an expert in bioinformatics, and it has worked with similar crop data before.
3.4 Resources to be committed 
 
BUDGET: 
The overall consortium during the four years of the proposed project (from the first hybridizations t o the final field 
assays, Figures 2 and 4 ) has an estimation of 4 .608.975 Euros total cost. We have allocated in real value more resources to 
those teams in charge of laboratory and field trials and tried to maximize the amount of staff engaged in these ex periments to 
ensure the data needed in this proposal.

 4.1. Participants (applicants) 
 
Participant name: Salvador Nogués 
Participant organization name: Universitat de Barcelona (UB) 
Description of legal entity and its main 
tasks, with an explanation of how its 
profile matches the tasks in the 
proposal:  
The University of Barcelona (UB) was founded in 1450. Today it boasts of a 
student body of 63,020 and a research staff of 5,312 members. Degrees are offered 
in 73 different areas of teaching with numerous postgraduate an d doctorate 
programs as well as continuing education courses. The University of Barcelona 
(UB) is the largest of the six universities of Barcelona and of the ten in Catalonia. 
The UB is ranked the first Spanish university, and the twenty third European 
institutions in scientific quality and productivity. The Department of Plant Biology of 
the UB is the oldest in Spain with Plant Physiology as a discipline and has a long 
experience on the photosynthetic mechanisms, the ecophysiology of plant 
productivity and  the identification of selection criteria for cereals under 
Mediterranean conditions. 
The UB manages in average 150 European projects per  year, for an amount of 
about 8,6 million euro  a year. Since 2002, the Department of Plant Biology of the 
UB has been coordinated the EC project: OPTICHINA (FP7-KBBE-2010-4 266045) 
Jose Luis Araus; and has been participating on several EC projects: SUSTAIN 
(QLKS-CT-2001-01461) Jose Luis Araus; MABDE (ICA3 -CT-2002-10026) Jordi 
Bort; IDuWUE (ICA3- CT-2002-10028) Jordi Bort; T RITIMED (INCO -CT-2004-
509136) Jordi Bort; PERMED (INCO -CT-2004-509140) Salvador Nogués; 
WATNITMED (INCO-CT-2004-509107) Salvador Nogués; OPTIWHEAT (INCO –T-
2006-015460) José Luis Araus; MELIA (INCO -CT-2006-517612) José Luis Araus; 
VITAL (FNC2008D) Salvador Nogués; SIBAE (COST ES0806) Salvador Nogués 
and OPTIMA (FP7-KBBE-2011-5) Salvador Nogués. 
The University of Barcelona develops all its activities related to the research in 
Europe through its European Research Projects Office, a unit in charge of the 
promotion of EC programmes, technical assistance to the elaboration of proposals 
and management of projects with participation of researchers of the UB, 
coordinated by the Vice -rector for Innovation and Transfer of Knowledge. Since 
January 2010, Universitat de Barcelona is part of the prestigious League of 
European Universities Research (LERU).  Fundació Bosch i Gimpera (FBG) is a 
third party of Universitat de Barcelona (UB). FBG was created and is controlled by 
UB, and  has an a uthorisation to a dminister International f unds on behalf of UB. 
According to the “Annotated General G rant Agreement”, FBG f alls u nder the 
specific case “Foundations, spin-off companies, etc., created in order to handle the 
administrative/financial tasks of the beneficiary”, and  it’s in charge of the 
administrative and financial management of European projects at the UB. FBG does 
not perform scientific/technical work in the project. 
Curriculum vitae:  The Plant Physiology Unit at the Department of Plant Biology (DPB) has more than 
30 years o f experience in RTD in plant physiology, molecular and biochemistry 
studies. 
Dr. S. Nogués (Male, M) is Associated Professor in Plant Physiology at DPB. He is 
specialist in metabolomics (carbon and n itrogen metabolisms in cereals  using 
stable isotopes) and plant responses to abiotic (including salt) and biotic stresses.  
He has participated in 12  EU-funded projects, 16 national projects and 3 contracts 
with private companies and regional administration. He has published more than 70 
scientific papers and 13 international book chapters.  
Prof. J. Azcón-Bieto (M) is Full Professor in Plant Physiology at DPB. He is a well-
known specialist of plant responses to C limate Change. He has participated in 15 
national projects. He has published 54 papers in SCI journals , 3 books in Plant 
Physiology and 35 international book chapters.

NEURICE    4 
 
Participant name: Blanca San Segundo 
Participant organization name: Centre for Research in Agricultural Genomics (CRAG)  
Description of legal entity and its main 
tasks, with an explanation of how its 
profile matches the tasks in the 
proposal: 
The Centre for Research in Agricultural Genomics, ( CRAG) is an independent 
research Institution that originated in 2003, established as a Consortium that 
includes the Spanish National Research Council (Consejo Superior de 
Investigaciones Científicas, CSIC), Institute of Agrifood Research and Technology 
(Institut de Recerca i Tecnologia Agroalimentàries, IRTA), Autonomous University of 
Barcelona (Universitat Autònoma de Barcelona, UAB), and University of Barcelona 
(Universitat de Barcelona, UB). CRAG is devoted to leading -edge research in the 
study of molecular and genetic characters of interest in plants and farm animals and 
in the application of molecular approaches for breeding of species important for 
agriculture and food production. Research at CRAG spans from primarily research 
of excellence in basic science (e.g. CSIC) to applied stu dies in collaboration with 
industry (e.g. IRTA, whose purpose is to contribute to the modernization and 
sustainable development of agriculture and food sectors).  
CRAG has been awarded "Human Resources Excellence in Research -HRS4R" - 
European Commission (http://www.cragenomica.es/human-resources-strategy-for-
researchers). 
CRAG is partner in BIOVEGEN (Spanish Technology  Platform for Plant 
Biotechnology), a private -public cooperation network for Research and 
Development involving stakeholders from industry, academia and the farming 
community in the field of Plant Biotechnology. 
Curriculum vitae: Dr. B . San Segundo (F) has more than 25 -years experience in plant molecular 
biology. The research goal at BSS’ group is to understand the molecular 
mechanisms involved in the plant response to environmental stress (biotic and 
abiotic stress), and ultimately to develop effective me ans for crop protection. 
Breakthroughs have been made in signalling  pathways and regulation of stress -
associated genes in rice plants, including sensing systems, initiation and 
maintenance of the host response, signal transduction pathways and effector 
elements in the plant response, and crosstalk events between biotic (pathogen 
infection) and abiotic (salinity, drought) stress. The functional analysis of genes 
identified at BSS’s laboratory has led to the identification of positive and negative 
regulators in salt tolerance in rice. 
Publications: 75 articles in International Journals (SCI), 8 Book Chapters (2 more in 
press), and 11 technical/scientific dissemination articles.  H-index: 28 (list of 
publications available at http://www.researcherid.com/rid/C-2417-2009). Invited 
Speaker in 40 International Congresses/Workshops. More than 30 
Seminars/conferences. Supervisor of 14 Ph.D. Thesis (4 more in progress) and 24 
Master Thesis. 
Dr. M. Coca (F) staff scientist from CSIC (“Científico Titular”), also has experience 
in plant molecular biology and adaptive responses to biotic and abiotic stress in rice. 
MC was partner in a Plant-KBBE project (Spain-France-Germany) for the production 
and accumulation of antimicrobial peptides in rice. 
Sonia Campo (F) is a Marie Curie  Postdoctoral Researcher integrated in the study 
of plant response to environmental stress at the BSS research group.

Participant name: Brigitte Courtois 
Participant organization name: Centre de Coopération Internationale en Recherche Agronomique pour le

Description of legal entity and its main

The Centre de Coopération Internationale en Recherche Agronomique pour le 
Développement (CIRAD) is a French agricultural r esearch centre conducting 
research for development in collaboration with developing countries. It employs 
1820 people and has an annual operating budget of 200 million Euros. About 60 
scientists are working on rice. CIRAD has a long standing collaboration with rice 
growing countries in the area of genetic improvement and is permanently involved 
in research programs dealing with rice varietal improvement, notably for tolerance 
to abiotic stresses.  
Its Genetic Improvement and Adaptation of Mediterranean and Tropical Crops Unit 
(UMR AGAP) has been involved in European projects dealing with the improvement 
of European rice and was notably in charge of the work packages on the 
improvement of rice salinity tolerance in EURIGEN and GreenRice projects. UMR 
AGAP has a long experience in using molecular markers for genetic analyses and 
marker-assisted breeding projects and, recently, started using them for genomic 
selection. 
Curriculum vitae:  Three permanent members of UMR AGAP will participate in NEURICE: 
Dr. B. Courtois (F) is a senior rice breeder and molecular geneticist with 30 years 
of experience, mostly in rice. She is presently working on association mapping for 
tolerance to abiotic stresses (drought, salinity) in the Rice Development and 
Adaptation team of U MR AGAP. She has published 80 papers in international 
journals. 
Dr. N. Ahmadi (M) is a senior plant breeder and molecular geneticist with 35 years 
of experience in rice. He is in charge of the Varietal Innovation Team of UMR AGAP 
and is coordinating all CI RAD rice breeding activities. He is also CIRAD 
representative in the Global Rice Science Partnership (GRiSP) Program Planning 
and Management Team. 
Axel Labeyrie  (M) is a junior rice breeder, member of the Varietal Innovation 
Team, based in Arles, in French  Camargue, and developing a joint rice breeding 
program for European rice in collaboration with Arnaud Boisnard at Centre Français 
du Riz.

The Consiglio per la Ricerca in Agricoltura e l’Analisi dell’Economia Agraria 
(CRA) is a National Research Organization which operates under the supervision of 
the Ministry of Agriculture, with general scientific competence within the fields of 
agriculture, agroin dustry, food, fishery and forestry. The distribution of the CRA 
offices throughout national territory allows it to widely extend its expertise and 
proficiency, and to closely operate in conjunction with central administrations, local 
and regional instituti ons, companies and various trade, industrial and legal 
associations. 
Curriculum vitae:  Dr. G. Valè (M) is in charge director of the CRA -RIS. His expertise  are related to 
plant-pathogens interaction studies that include map -based cloning of disease 
resistance genes in barley, identification and mapping of disease resistance genes 
in barley, durum wheat and rice. Research activities also include the development 
of a physical map for bread wheat chromosome 5A, identification and mapping of 
useful traits in e ggplant and evaluation of rice germplasm for agronomical relevant 
traits to be used in association mapping studies. He has participated to 18 national 
and 2 international projects as responsible of research unit and was coordinator in 2 
national projects. He has published more than 100 publications, 41 in ISI-WoS. 
Dr. L. Cattivelli (M) has a degree in Agricultural Science at the Catholic University 
of Piacenza (1986). LC worked at the Max Planck Institute of Cologne (Germany, 
1987-1989), and at the Experime ntal Institute for Cereal Research of Fiorenzuola 
d’arda (Italy 1990 - 2005). Professor in Plant Genetics at the University of Verona 
(1997-2003), from 2005 to 2009 LC has been director of the CRA -Cereal Research 
Centre in Foggia and from 2010 is director o f the CRA-Genomics Research Centre 
in Fiorenzuola d’Arda. LC is member of in the coordinating committee of the 
International Wheat Genome Sequencing Consortium (IWGSC), Italian 
representative in the research committee of the Wheat Initiative, member of the  
editorial boards of “Plant Science” and of “Journal of Cereal Science”. 
Dr. A. Tondelli (M) is researcher at CRA-GPG. The research activity of Alessandro 
Tondelli is mainly dedicated to the genetic dissection of quantitative traits through 
linkage and ass ociation mapping approaches, in different cereal crop species 
including rice, barley and wheat. In particular, research works focus on several 
aspects of plant adaptation to the environment, such as tolerance to low 
temperatures, regulation of plant phenol ogy and morphology, yield adaptation to 
Mediterranean conditions, plant biomass and straw -related traits for energy 
conversion. In the RISINNOVA project, association mapping for different agronomic 
traits has been carried out in a large rice germplasm coll ection. He has participated 
to 2 national and 4 EU -funded projects and published 20 manuscripts on peer -
reviewed journals. 
Dr. G. Tacconi (M) is researcher at CRA-GPG since 2001. PhD in Biotechnology in 
2004, Master Degree in Biotechnology at University of  Verona in 1999. Research 
works focus on:  molecular breeding and MAS in barley and rice; diseases 
resistances and plant -pathogen interaction in barley, rice, wheat, kiwifruit; 
phenotyping of root development in rice and barley; transcriptome analysis. He i s 
involved in DROPSA EU project for plant -pathogen interaction. He was involved in 
RISINNOVA project for mapping of new disease resistance loci and marker -
assisted selection and for genome wide association studies for root traits in rice. He 
has published 17 manuscripts on peer-reviewed journals. 
Dr. M. Stefano (M) is researcher at CRA-RIS. His main research topic is the study 
of the fate of carbon and nitrogen in agro -ecosystems (nitrates leaching, ammonia 
emissions, soil carbon changes), using laboratory,  field and modelling approaches. 
He has been involved in consulting activity in the field of agronomy and

Committee of the Piemonte Region in Italy and at the Northern Italy inter -regional 
working group for the designing the request from Italy for a derogation to the Nitrate 
Directive. He has published 8 papers in ISI journals and 12 technical publications.

CRA participates to this project with two research stations: the Rice research unit 
(CRA-RIS) and the Genomics Research Centre (CRA-GPG).  
CRA-RIS is devoted to research on rice genetics and breeding for tolerance to 
biotic and abiotic stresses and gr ain quality parameters. CRA -RIS has 30 Ha of 
experimental fields located in the main rice growing areas and possess different rice 
genetic resources including a large rice germplasm collection, a TILLING population 
and several recombinant inbred lines (RIL
s) populations segregating for different 
agronomical relevant traits (including salt tolerance). CRA -RIS has the small farm 
equipment necessary for all operations (sowing, harvesting, threshing, drying) to 
growth rice and for conducting pre- and post-harvest phenotyping.  
CRA-GPG has expertise in molecular biology, bioinformatics, genetic and genomics 
on barley, rice and wheat, with a specific focus on biotic and abiotic stress 
resistance and yield and quality-related traits, QTLs identification, positional cloning 
of genes, transcriptomic and functional genomics. The Centre applies genome-wide 
association scans and genomic selection in barley, rice and wheat. The Centre has 
a fully equipped laboratory for plant genomics and bioinformatics; growth chambers, 
green houses, an experimental farm of 16 ha.

Participant name: Gian Attilio Sacchi  
Participant organization name: Università degli Studi di Milano (UMIL) 
Description of legal entity and its main

The University of Milano  (UMIL) is a public teaching and research University, 
which - with 8 faculties and 2 schools and a teaching staff of 2000 professors -  is 
distinguished by its wide variety of disciplinary fields. The Depa rtment of 
Agricultural and Environmental Sciences -  Production, Land, Agroenergy (DiSAA) 
develops its activities with a view to advancement through scientific research, 
knowledge about farming systems, forestry, livestock, environment and energy 
based on a multidisciplinary approach aimed at promotion of effective and efficient 
management of complex agricultural systems.  
Research at the DiSAA Division of Plant Production aims at improving crop 
productivity and sustainability applying approaches ranging fro m a macroscopic 
level-system to the molecular level, including the use of both traditional and 
innovative biotechnological methods (molecular biology, genomics, proteomics, 
metabolomics, ionomics, system biology). The group around Prof. G.A. Sacchi at 
DiSAA is working since many years on plant physiology, biochemistry and 
molecular biology topics devoted to plant mineral nutrition and responses to abiotic 
stress. Recently the group developed ionomic and metabolomic approaches 
adopting ICP -MS, GC -MS, LC -ESI-MS/MS, and NMR techniques, and their 
informatics-based overlap, with the aim to evaluate the effects and the molecular 
bases of different paddy field managements (water and fertilizers) on quantitative 
and qualitative aspect of rice yield, with particular regards to grain nutritional value 
(density in microelements and vitamins) and safety (absence of toxic trace 
elements as Cd, As and Pb). 
Curriculum vitae:  Dr. G. A. Sacchi (M) is Full Professor of Agricultural Chemistry at UMIL -DiSAA. 
Topics of his rese arch are: a) molecular, biochemical and physiological aspects of 
plant mineral nutrition and response to abiotic stresses; b) molecular and 
biochemical basis of uptake, accumulation, toxicity and detoxification of organic and 
inorganic pollutants in plants ; c) ionomic and metabolomics approaches for food 
security and safety. He is authors of 45 articles in peer -reviewed international 
journals, several book chapters and many conference papers. 
He is the coordinator of the “Plant Ionomics Lab” of UMIL -DiSAA. He has been 
group leader in the following national and international research programs: a) Life 
Environment Project LIFE99 ENV/IT/0078 PhyLeS : Phytoextraction of Le ad from 
Soil - PHYLES”; b) Prin -MiUR (1997- 2009); c) Regione Lombardia “Safety and

water and carbon fluxes in Mays agro -system – AC-CA (2009.2011); e) AGER -
Foundation “Integrated genetic and genomic approaches for new Italian rice 
breeding strategies - RISINNOVA” (2011-2014); f) MiPAAF “Research, innovative 
technologies, environmental sustainability for the improvement of Italian rice -  
POLORISO” (2012 -2015); g) UE -FP7 Marie Curie Initial Training Network  
“Biochemical and Genetic Dissection of Control of Plant Mineral N utrition - 
BIONUT" (2011-2014). He has been scientific coordinator of the projects: a) Banca

Participant name: Michael Blatt  
Participant organization name: University of Glasgow (UGLA) 
Description of legal entity and its main 
tasks, with an explanation of how its 
profile matches the tasks in the 
proposal:  
After Oxford, Cambridge and Durham, the University of Glasgow  (UGLA) is the 
fourth oldest higher -education institution in t he English -speaking world. It is a 
member of the elite Russell Group of universities in the UK, a founding member of 
the Scottish Universities Life Science Alliance (SULSA) and of Universitas -21, an 
international consortium of universities setting standard s for higher education 
globally. The University of Glasgow caters for some 22,000 undergraduate and 
postgraduate students, roughly 6000 of whom are enrolled within the College of 
Medical, Veterinary and Life Sciences. The College comprises some 300 full -time 
academic and research staff and over 500 postdoctoral researchers and 
technicians. It maintains close research and teaching connections with a several 
associated centres situated around Glasgow, including the Beatson Institute of 
Cancer Research, the Mo redun Institute of Animal Research, and the James 
Hutton Institute (Dundee), and it operates the Scottish Centre for Ecology and the 
Natural Environment (SCENE) based at nearby Loch Lomond.  
The Institute of Molecular, Cell and Systems Biology (MCSB), to w hich Prof. Blatt 
and six other Plant Science Group (PSG) staff belong, is one of five premier 
research institutes within the College and accounts for 35% of the annual €50M 
research income to the College. Overall Glasgow currently attracts over €160M in 
research income annually, making it one of the top ten centres  for academic 
research in the UK. The University of Glasgow provides a number of underpinning 
support services beyond the standard financial management, estates and 
maintenance services. Among the se, MRB works closely with the Research and 
Enterprise Office, and has drawn on their expertise in expanding technological 
applications within the commercial sector as well as establishing research and pre -
commercial interactions. MRB has developed links w ith industrial/technology 
transfer partners (Agrisera, Dualsystems, Plant Bioscience) and research institutes 
(James Hutton Institute, the John Innes Centre in Norwich). 
Curriculum vitae:  Prof. M.R. Blatt (M) is the Regius Professor of Botany and Head of Plant Sciences 
at Glasgow. His Laboratory of Plant Physiology and Biophysics is one of a handful 
of centres worldwide at the frontiers of research in plant membrane biology. He has 
long researched closely related themes of membrane biophysics, signalling  and 
cellular homeostasis in plants, much of this work on stomatal guard cells and ion 
channels. He originally defined the characteristics of intact guard cells, including the 
roles for extracellular K + and cytosolic pH in K + channel control. His laboratory  
identified the coupling of Ca 2+ oscillations to membrane voltage, its relationship to 
ABA and voltage-gated Ca2+ channels at the plasma membrane, its integration with 
endomembrane Ca 2+ release as well as critical binding sites for reactive oxygen 
species mediating channel regulation. He developed the first quantitative systems 
model for guard cell membrane transport and homeost asis with real predictive 
power and is currently engaged in a major research project to expand this model to 
the field. 
MRB also st udies the coordination of vesicle traffic with ion transport for cell 
expansion. He discovered the syntaxin SYP121 (=SYR1/PEN1) of tobacco and 
Arabidopsis, demonstrating its role in signalling and ion channel control. His 
laboratory found that SYP121, and its homologues in other species, binds plant Kv 
(K+) channels, regulating their gating for K + uptake and growth via binding sites on 
the two proteins. MRB recently identified the Sec1/Munc18 (SM) protein SEC11 as 
a regulatory partner with SYP121 in its SNA RE cycle], and he addressing the 
regulatory role of Kv channel binding exchange as a key step in the control of 
vesicle fusion and K+ transport control.  
MRB has contributed directly to economic competitiveness and quality of life 
through agro-industrial applications of research, including IPR development through 
patents (UK 9720784.9, 9720785.6, Intnl. Patent WO 99/16880, US Patent 
6,821,735), education and research training. MRB continues to develop a range of 
methods for multiprotein interaction and in v ivo trafficking analysis all of which are 
available through the laboratory website. Some will find application i n this project. 
The laboratory is among a small number of sites worldwide pushing the frontiers of 
knowledge in plant membrane biology, biophysi cs and cellular signalling. MRB 
trains some the best researchers in these fields, and has attracted research visitors

from around the world (in past 10 years, including students, fellows and sabbatical 
visitors from within the UK as well as Spain, Germany,  Italy, Mexico, France,

staff and students have gone on to substantive posts, including within Imp erial 
College London, Universities of Cork, Dundee, Seville, Sydney (Australia), Louvain 
(Belgium), Tübingen, and Salzburg, as well as management and industrial

Participant name: Mar Català

Description of legal entity and its main

The Institut de Recerca i Tecnologia Agroalimentària (IRTA) is a public 
research institution, part of the Department of Agriculture, Food and Rural Action of 
the regional  Government of Catalonia, Spain. IRTA's mission is to contribute to 
modernizing, improving, boosting competitiveness, and fostering sustainable 
development in the sectors of: i) agriculture, ii) animal and plant production, iii) food 
technology, iv) agroforestry, v) aquaculture, vi) fisheries, vii) agro -food economy 
and vii) environment and global change, with the aim of consolidating a sustainable 
bio-based economy. Other areas of activity are those which are directly or indirectly 
related to the supply of  healthy, high -quality foodstuffs to end consumers, food 
safety and safe processing of foodstuffs and in general enhancing the health and 
well-being of the population. Ebr o Experimental Station, located in the Ebro  Delta 
area, was created in 1987 with the main objective to promote rice competitiveness, 
focusing on innovation, experimentation and knowledge and technology transfer to 
rice producers. During this period it has become the reference centre  for the rice 
sector in the area. 
Curriculum vitae:  Mar Catalá (F), leader of rice research at Ebre Experimental Station (IRTA), is 
secretary of the National Rice Agronomy and Breeding Group since 1996, Group

Participant name: María Mercedes Rivero Pérez 
Participant organization name: Instituto de Agrobiotecnología Rosario (INDEAR) 
Description of legal entity and its main 
tasks, with an explanation of how its 
profile matches the tasks in the 
proposal:  
The Instituto de Agrobiotecnología Rosario (INDEAR)  is a new model for the 
strategic integration between the Argentine National Council for Scientific and 
Technical Research (CONICET) and the private sector in the scientific -technology 
field, where CONICET contributes with qualified research resources and INDEAR 
provides funds, management and competences for the technology transference. 
The intention of this approach is to deliver financial value and social benefit through 
the development of products and services in the agricultural biotechnology industry. 
INDEAR has the most advanced agro -biotech research platforms in Latin America, 
including the first high performance DNA sequencing platform available in 
Argentina. INDEAR labs host highly qualified scientific groups in the areas of 
genomics and b ioinformatics, molecular biology, synthetic biology and protein 
research. R&D areas at the Institute are consolidated with a plant transformation 
and tissue culture facility and with a multidisciplinary group engaged in the 
development of field technologie s. Furthermore, INDEAR has a prestigious team 
devoted to regulatory affairs, working on its different projects. INDEAR devotes its 
research efforts in technologies designed to increase crop yield, including drought 
and salinity tolerance, pest and herbicide resistance, efficient use of nutrients, and 
crop health.  
The Genomics and Bioinformatics platform of our Institution is equipped with two 
high performance sequencing systems which are complementary to each other: 
454 GS FLX+ Roche and Illumina HiSeq 150 0. The specialized support staff not 
only conducts internal research projects at INDEAR and collaboration work, but 
also provides sequencing services to various universities and national / 
international research centres. From the sequencing of complex plant genomes, the 
processing of thousands of metagenomic environmental samples significant work in 
bacterial and viral genomes, to the addressing of transcriptomic studies and health -
related projects, the Genomics team is constantly busy delivering valuable 
contributions in the form of massive data of high quality DNA sequences. The 
sequencing activities are supported by the Bioinformatics department and its highly 
trained team in the scientific and technical arena, with deep expertise in Biology, 
Computing an d Stats. Data are processed by a sophisticated system including 
automated pipelines for sequence quality control, assembly, annotation, and 
manual support tools for finishing and annotation.  
Our Molecular Biology platform is composed by a group of experie nced 
professionals and technicians. The main tasks of this Laboratory are to design and 
build binary vectors intended for plant transformation, the molecular -level analysis 
of the transgenic events generated, and the identification of genes of interest and  
regulatory sequences.  
Our Plant Transformation Laboratory has the ability to transform numerous plant 
species such as soybean, alfalfa, maize, rice, safflower, switchgrass , as well as 
other model plant species. We have focused on generating freedom to operate  
efficient transformation technologies. Besides, we apply complementary techniques 
such as multiplication and micropropagation of selected materials (GM events, 
mother plants, elite  materials), rescue of embryos and generation of doubled 
haploid lines for the accelerated development of new varieties in wheat and maize.  
INDEAR also has an important Field Testing and Breeding area that applies the 
most advanced breeding techniques to wheat, soybean, corn and alfalfa crops. The 
main role of this platform  is to validate technologies in breeding chamber, 
greenhouse and field conditions. The assessment of the technologies delivered via 
transgenesis requires the adherence to stringent biosecurity protocols; to that end, 
we have a sound, expert Regulatory Affa irs team. On the Metabolic Engineering 
platform of our Institute genetically optimized organisms are developed for the 
production of high valued -added and minimum environmental impact compounds 
from low cost raw materials.

Description of any significant 
infrastructure and/or any major items 
of technical equipment, relevant to the 
proposed work:  
  
INDEAR is a model research Institute with several platforms and laboratories: 
Genomics and Bioinformatics, Molecular Biology, Metabolic Engineering, 
Technology of  proteins; Plant Transformation and Tissue Culture; Plant Breeding 
and Field Testing and a Pilot Plant for Molecular Farming. 
The Genomics and Bioinformatics platform of Indear is equipped with two high -
performance sequencing complementary systems: a 454 s equencer of Roche 
(Genome Sequencer FLX System) and HiSeq 1500 Illumina sequencer. It is the 
only platform of its kind in the country. Illumina HiSeq1500 technology offers a 
unique combination of high performance and exceptional accuracy; therefore it is 
suitable for large -scale genomics projects. For the analysis of 16S rRNA we 
dispose of a Benchtop NGS (Next Generation Sequencing) -  MiSeq Illumina. This 
technology allows smaller-scale, shorter runs and best accuracy at lower costs. At 
the Lab we also have  an automatic production system of clonal clusters for 
sequencing (Illumina cBOT), an Agilent BioAnalyzer 2100 so as to quantify, to 
control quality and to determine DNA, RNA, proteins, and cells size; an Agilent 
SureScan reader of microarrays; a fluoresce nce reader in microplate (FLUOstar 
best); a Beckman particle counter; a fragmentator system of DNA Digilab Hydro 
Shear; a system of real -time PCR (LightCycler 480 Roche); a system of mills for 
mechanical disruption for bacteria (TissueLyser QIAGEN); a cent rifugal 
concentrator, necessary for the preparation of libraries of next generation 
sequencing (HiSeq 1500/MiSeq Illumina and GS FLX Roche). This platform also 
includes a server room equipped with 2 HPC clusters with 96 cores in 12 nodes and 
a server of 8 cores and 32 GB of RAM. 
The Molecular Biology platform has the necessary instruments for basic genetic 
engineering: cloning of DNA sequences, bacterial transformation and molecular 
characterization of bacterial organisms. There are also equipments for Quantitative 
PCR (LightCycler 480), real time PCR and an automated liquid handling station 
(Lifor quid Handling Biomek 3000) for large scale experiments and routine work.  
The laboratory of Proteins and the Metabolic Engineering platform have the basic 
equipment required for isolation and functional characterization of proteins such as 
an AKTA chromatography equipment and an ultrafiltration equipment. These areas 
also have equipment for liquid chromatography associated to a mass spectrometer 
(Triple quadruple -LC-MSMS), equipment for gas chromatography with mass 
spectroscopy (GC -MS), a lyophilizer, an autoclave and an UV detector for the 
analysis of samples. It also has a fully automated New Brunswick 3 liters 
fermentator for the scaling-up of fermentation laboratory processes.  
The platform for Plat Transformation and Tissue Culture has 6 laminar -flow double-
cabinets, 8 growthrooms for in vitro  culture of plants with automated and 
independent control of temperature and photoperiod; independent growth chambers 
with humidity control; microscopes equipped with high resolution camera; automatic 
dispenser of media and other minor equipment. There are also greenhouse facilities 
and instruments for carrying out experimental analysis in plants.

Participant name: Jiankang Wang 
Participant organization name: Chinese Academy of Agricultural Sciences -  Institute of Crop Sciences 
(CAAS) 
Description of legal entity and its main 
tasks, with an explanation of how its 
profile matches the tasks in the 
proposal:  
Institute of C rop Science (ICS) is the largest professional crop science institute 
affiliated to the Chinese Academy of Agricultural Sciences (CAAS) . ICS has four 
departments on Genetic Resources, Molecular Biology, Crop Breeding and Crop 
Physiology. There are 40 resear ch groups in the four departments to work on 
wheat, maize, rice, soybean, and many other small crops. ICS is the national centre 
of China for scientific innovations, international collaborations, and advanced 
educations. Currently, ICS has more than 300 st affs, among which there are 83 
professors.  
The Chinese Academy of Agricultural Sciences (CAAS) is a national agricultural 
research institution undertaking China’s agricultural research and development in 
both basic and applied sciences as well as new and advanced application 
technology. Mission of CAAS is to solve the fundamental and strategic 
technological issues in agriculture and rural economic development, training of 
advanced researchers, integration of agriculture with science and technology, and 
development of agricultural science and technology exchanges and cooperation. 
CAAS achieves this mission through its various research institutes, graduate 
school, agricultural publisher, key laboratories, testing centres, crop improvement 
centres, technology centres, crop germplasm banks, databases and Internet 
resources.  
Curriculum vitae:  
 
 
 
 
 
Dr. Wang is a Professor in the Institute of Crop Science, CAAS. His research team 
at CAAS has 4 research staffs, and about 10 MSc and PhD students, mainly 
working on the following three areas.  
a) Genetic Analysis Methods in Plants: Inclusive Composite Interval Mapping 
(ICIM) for additive and digenic epistatic QTL of quantitative traits were 
proposed in 2006 and 2007. ICIM is computationally less intensive, and has 
increased detection power, reduced false discovery rate, and less biased 
estimates of QTL effects. This method has been extended to F2 population, 
NAM population, and QTL by environmental analysis, and is being extended to 
other multi-parental genetic populations.  
b) Modeling and Simulation in Plant Breeding: The genetics and breeding tool of 
QuLine he developed can simulate most breeding methodologies for 
developing inbred lines. QuLine has been used to compare two different 
selection strategies in CIMMYT’s wheat  breeding programs, study the effects 
on selection of dominance and epistasis, predict cross performance using 
known gene information in wheat quality, and optimize marker assisted 
selection to efficient pyramid multiple genes. The other two tools are QuHy brid 
for simulating hybrid development breeding, and QuMARS for simulating 
marker assisted recurrent selection.  
c) Integrated Genetics and Breeding Tool: QTL IciMapping is freely -available 
public software, capable of building high -density linkage genetic map s and 
mapping quantitative trait loci (QTL). Version 3.3 of the software was released 
in July 2013. Eight fully implemented functionalities in QTL IciMapping v3.3 
are: (1) BIN: Binning of redundant markers; (2) MAP: Construction of genetic 
linkage maps in biparental populations; (3) BIP: Mapping of additive and 
digenic epistasis genes in biparental populations; (4) CSL: Mapping of additive 
and digenic epistasis genes with chromosome segment substitution lines; (5) 
MET: QTL by environment interaction in bipa rental populations; (6) NAM: QTL 
mapping in nested association mapping populations; (7) SDL: Mapping of 
segregation distortion loci in biparental populations; and (8) CMP: Consensus 
map construction from multiple genetic linkage maps sharing common 
markers. Two supplementary tools are: (1) 2pointREC: Estimation of 
recombination frequency between two loci in 20 biparental populations; and (2) 
ANOVA: Analysis of variance of multi-environmental trials.  
In addition to research, Dr. Wang has been teaching the Q uantitative Genetics 
Course to the CAAS Graduate School since 2005. Each year, he has 50 -70 
graduate students in his class. A textbook in Chinese was published in 2007. He

started to teach the Experimental Design and Statistical Analysis for foreigner 
students at the CAAS Graduate School since 2012.

Participant name: Xavier Serrat

The Càmara Arrossera de l Montsià (CAMARA)  is a rice farmer cooperative 
founded in 1927, bringing together 3200 partners and their rice production, which is 
manufactured and marketed under the PDO “Arroz del Delta del Ebro”. It is the only 
Cooperative that has received twice the recognition from the LIFE EU program for 
the respect to the environment. CAMARA has obtained the most demanding 
certifications in terms of food security as a result of their efforts to innovate and 
improve product quality. The R+D team focus their efforts to modernize the seed 
development section, which ensures high quality rice seed varieties distribution to 
CAMARA farmers and other Spanish rice Cooperatives. CAMARA is the biggest 
farmer cooperative in Delta del Ebro and produce and commercialize certified  
seeds all over Spain while is constantly breeding and registering new rice varieties.

finishing his PhD in Applied Biotechnology on Mediterranean rice cultivars, he has

Participant name: Arnaud Boisnard 
Participant organization name: Centre Français du Riz (CFR) 
Description of legal entity and its main

proposal:  
Centre Fr ançais du Riz  (CFR) is the French technical institute created in 1985 
whose aim is to conduct research and extension work on rice. It is based in the 
heart of the French rice growing area, and is headed by a committee composed of 
farmers, rice industrials and scientists. It has close links with both upstream and 
downstream sectors: INRA, CIRAD, rice growers, rice industries, and food 
companies. It employs 8 people working on several programs: agronomy and 
environment, crop protection, breeding, grain quality. Since 2001, it registered more 
than 20 new rice varieties through its rice breeding program. In NEURICE project, 
CFR will be responsible for salinity tolerant improved rice line development and 
field trials conducted in France. Salinity tolerant varieti es are expected to be 
obtained at the end of NEURICE project for a future registration and 
commercialization to the Camargue and European farmers. CFR will also contribute 
in communication to the public, through the organization of a farmers’ field day, 
named «  Les Prémices du Riz », the annual reports to the rice farmers named 
“Bilan de Campagne”, and to the scientific community. 
CFR has more than 30 years of experience in RTD in rice agronomy and breeding. 
Curriculum vitae:  Dr A. Boisnard (M) is rice br eeder at CFR. He is responsible of the rice breeding 
program for Camargue conducted in collaboration with CIRAD. He has more than 
10 years of experience in rice quantitative genetics (molecular genotyping, QTL 
analyses, QTL fine mapping) and breeding (high -throughput phenotyping, 
conventional breeding, marker -assisted breeding). He participated to national and 
international projects, like a Genoplante project on rice partial resistance to Rice 
yellow mottle virus, a BBSRC -SARID project on Striga resistance in cereals, and 
the European project GreenRice on an alternative wetting and drying system to 
reduce greenhouse emission and water consumption during rice growing. 
Cyrille Thomas (M) is agronomist at CFR. He has more than 15 years of 
experience in rice, re sponsible of the agronomy and crop protection programs. He 
participated to national and European projects like the FranceAgriMer annual 
projects, FACCE-ERA-NET+ European project GreenRice, ADEME project Eco -C-
Réal.

The Società Italiana Sementi Spa (SIS) was set up in 1947 with the aim of taking 
care of the multiplication of the certified seed obtained by public and private 
breeders for different species. Now t he Company is controlled by Producer’s 
Cooperatives of North, Centre and South of Italy and deals with different species 
(wheat, rice, maize, prote -oleaginous crops, forage and turf grasses). Research 
(breeding) activities mainly concentrates on wheat (com mon and durum) and rice. 
Thanks to the collaboration and exchange of genetic material with public and 
private Research Centers in Italy and abroad, SIS carries out a continuous activity 
of germplasm evaluation and comparison. On wheat and rice the R&D team  
manages directly trials in different locations (5 for rice and 7 for wheat) around Italy. 
Post-
harvest test are done in the lab to evaluate the quality of tested genotypes 
with different microtest (e.g.: milling yield evaluation, RVA analysis, yellow inde x, 
gluten index, protein content, SDS sedimentation test, electrophoresis of protein). 
The Company participate to different research projects in collaboration with public 
and private research groups.

Italy and abroad.

(Articles 11 and 12 of the General Model Grant Agreement) 
Yes 
Fundació Bosch i Gimpera (FBG) (Bosch i Gimpera Foundation, http://www.fbg.ub.edu) is a non -profit foundation and is 
considered a third party of Universitat de Barcelona (UB). FBG was created by UB in 1983, and is governed by a long lasting 
agreement signed between UB and FBG. According to the “Annotated General Grant Agreement” (art. 41.2), FBG is a UB third 
party that makes available some of its resources to the beneficiary for free, and falls under the specific case of “Foundatio ns, 
spin-off companies, etc., created in order to handle the administrative/financial tasks of the beneficiary” . Thus, FBG handles 
the financial and administrative aspects of the beneficiary UB involvement in research projects, including all issues relating to 
the employment and payment of additional personnel, purchase of equipment and consumables, etc. The person nel hired for 
the project by the foundation works on the premises of the beneficiary UB and under its responsibility. FBG does not carry ou t 
part of the work in the project, and no resources are allocated for FBG in the project. This will imply during the project that: 
 UB remains the beneficiary of the project and is thus responsible for the scientific and financial aspects of the project. 
 UB and FBG together complete the financial forms (Form C) needed for the management report when requested. 
FBG will prepare this Form C, which is signed by the authorised representative of the UB. 
 UB and FBG will prepare and submit Certificate on Financial Statements when applicable  following the current 
guidelines.

5.1 Ethics 
No ethic issue arises in the proposed project. Research will be conducted within EU-countries, namely France, Italy, United

their counties’ legal framework and also of the terms & conditions for their participation at the Research for the Benefit of SMEs 
or H2020 Calls. None of the Ethics Issues in the Table below is relevant to the proposed project.

contents and the actions proposed by the proposed NEURICE project proposal, corresponding to the
call ofSustainableFood Securityand the sub-call of H2020-SFS-2014-2015 and topic Strategies
forcropproductivity,stabilityand qualitySFS-05-2015,_witha closure date of11th June 2015. We
would like to express our highest appreciation of the project approach and targeted objectives.
Comunidad General de Regantes hereby expresses the intentto give support to the NEURICE
project.At Comunidad General de Regantes, we agree on the significance ofthe problems that are
addressed by the NEURICE project.We also see the need to improve soilorganic matter as a majar
priorityforthe European arable and horticulturesector.
Therefore,we have a serious interestinthe approach ofthe NEURICE thematic network to improving
identification,predictionand introductionofusefulgenetic variationincrops. We believe thisproject,if
successful, willindeed help to bring farmers, industryand researchers together to inprove while
seeking for novel breeding targets to improve yield,yield stability,quality,biotic/abioticstress
resistanceltolerance and environmental benefits.
Comunidad General de Regantes del Canal de la Derecha del Ebro is a non profitorganization
responsible forthe collection and distributionof water from the riverEbro to their almost 5.000
members irrigatorswho form part ofthe righthemidelta ofthe Ebro,as wellas ponds, bay and natural
areas ofthe Delta.A 90% ofitsland isoccupied by rice fields,reason forwhy isso important the rice
growing inour organization.
Also,as founder ofDeltamed, we are aware ofthe common problem problems faced by wetlands and
particularlythe deltas,such as the salinityinfields.
Comunidad General de Regantes isthereforeinterestedinthe NEURICE projectand would envisage
being involvedin helping the projectby:
Participatingto providefeedback and advice on salinitysoiltrials
Participating inthe proposed dissemination activities

2015,_with a closure date of11th June 2015. We would liketo express our highest appreciation ofthe
projectapproach and targeted objectives DELTAMED hereby expresses the intentto give supportto
the NEURICE project. At DELTAMED, we agree on the significance of the problems that are
addressed by the NEURICE project.We also see the need to improve soilorganic matter as a major
priorityforthe European arable and horticulturesector.
Therefore,we have a serious interestinthe approach ofthe NEURICE thematic network to improving
identification,predictionand introductionofusefulgenetic variation incrops. We believe thisproject,if
successful, willindeed help to bring farmers, industryand researchers together to inprove while
seeking for novel breeding targets to improve yield,yield stability,quality,biotic/abioticstress
resistance/tolerance and environmental benefits.
DELTAMED core business isinthe objectives ofthe Association are to constitutea permanent forum
in order to analyse, discuss and deal with the specific problems of a natural, water, coastal,
environmental, economic production and social nature concerning the Mediterranean deltas,
particularlywith a view to achieving sustainable development inthese deltas.Inaddition,itsoperations
can be extended to dealing with the problems involvingthe Coastal Wetlands ofthe Mediterranean
area where there are similar issues tothose which concern the deltas.

Participatingto providefeedback and advice on salinitysoiltrials

26/Os/201s
The organization Syndicot des Riziculteurs de France et Filière represented by its
President Bertrand MAZEL declares its interest in NEURICE project and wish to be
involved in the project as Associated Stakeholder, if the proposal is accepted for
funding by the European Commission.
The status Associated Stakeholder implies being regularly informed about the progress
of project, the practical results and planned activities. Our personnel will be
preferentially invited to the end-user conferences with reduced registration fee.
As Associated Stakeholder, the organization Syndicot des Riziculteurs de Fronce et
Filière will assist especially in the dissemination of the project results and the transfer
of knowledge generated within the NEURICE project, when this knowledge and results
are of potential interest to our associates or members.

The organization will also undertake a protective approach and keep all information
confidential that pertains to the structure as well as the technical content of the
proposal set-up. lt will only disclose said information to third parties upon the
coord inator's approval.

APARROZ – AGRUPAMENTO DE PRODUTORES DE ARROZ DO VALE DO SADO, LDA. 
         Rua do Arroz nº 1                                                               Tel.: 265 619180  
7580 - 161 Alcácer do Sal                                                             Fax. 265 619181

To Whom It May Concern 
 
 
 
APARROZ – Agrupamento de Produtores de Arroz do Vale do Sado, Portugal  expresses 
its deepest interest in the research project NEURICE (New commercial European RICE 
(Oryza sativa) harbouring salt tolerance alleles to protect the rice sector against climate 
change and apple snail ( Pomacea insularum ) invasion) (program  Horizon2020 Call 
“SUSTAINABLE FOOD SECURITY”), to be pursued in cooperation with UB (Spain), CRAG 
(Spain), CIRAD (France), CRA (Italy), UMIL (Italy), UGLA (Scotland), IRTA (Spain), 
INDEAR (Argentina), CAMARA (Spain), IRIS (Spain), CFR (France), CAAS (China), SIS 
(Italy) and its eagerness to be a non-academic Associated Partner of the project. 
The NEURICE framework may constitute a mission-critical part of APARROZ and its 
collection history. Participation in its support and development is therefore of strategic 
importance to us. 
We, at the APARROZ, commit ourselves to support the researchers involved in the 
project, granting all the needed facilities and accessibility to support the NEURICE project 
when deemed convenient by all parties.  The APARROZ is also most willing to facilitate 
and promote the dissemination and knowledge exchange connected to the project. 
APARROZ is keenly interested in the issues addressed by this Project and looks forward 
to its success as an excellent opportunity to enhance the cooperation between the 
institutions concerned. 
    
Your´s sincerely, 
    APARROZ – AGRUPAMENTO DE PRODUTORES 
DE ARROZ DO VALE DO SADO, LDA                  
Pelo Conselho de Gerência
